Case of French Sailors Shooting and Wounding Chinese Police in Hankou 55

Hankou Correspondence: A case of French sailors shooting and wounding Chinese police occurred at 9:50 PM on the 14th on Eryao Road in Special District One of this city. The details are as follows:

Cause of the Incident: At 9:50 PM on the night of the 14th, three French sailors had an argument with a rickshaw puller in front of the Bu Na Mao Foreign Firm on Eryao Road because they did not pay the full fare. Police Officer Zhang Guangyu, who was on duty in the area, went to mediate and waved the rickshaw puller away. Unexpectedly, the sailors beat the rickshaw puller. Not satisfied with that, they turned their anger on the police officer and punched him repeatedly. The police officer had no choice but to blow his whistle for assistance. The sailors then took out their pistols and fired three shots in a row, wounding police officers Liu Jinshan and Xia Jinshan. They then fired three more shots, and an American military policeman who was passing by was hit and injured in the limbs. He was admitted to the hospital. Police Officer Liu Jinshan suffered a severe injury to his right ankle bone, and Xia Jinshan was injured in the leg. Both were ordered by the head of the police station to be taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Zhang Guangyu's injuries were relatively minor because he was punched.

Arrest of Suspects: After the gunshots erupted, the area was in an uproar. Nearby shops closed their doors one after another. Chen Shiyong, the head of the police station, immediately telegraphed the Public Security Bureau and personally led a translator and chief police officer to the scene of the incident to investigate. Just then, Captain Jiang of the Public Security Bureau Security Team also led armed police officers to the scene and searched separately. They apprehended a French military officer, Head Keqin, and one sailor, and found a pistol and many bullets. They were immediately taken to the police station for custody. It was already 1:00 AM.

Demands of the French Consul: After the incident occurred, the French Consul, Bodes, personally went to Mayor Liu's residence late at night with Secretary You to negotiate. According to them, Head Keqin was the captain of a ship and was ordered to go to the scene to investigate after hearing that sailors were causing trouble on shore. He was not the perpetrator. They also said that the bullets that wounded the Chinese police were different from Head's bullets, indicating that Head was not the perpetrator. Mayor Liu carefully examined the bullets with Chief Chen and confirmed that the bullets were different, as the French Consul had said. The French Consul was then asked to write a letter of guarantee stating two points: (1) Head Keqin was the captain of a capital warship sent to investigate the case; (2) Head Keqin's bullets were different from the bullets that wounded the Chinese police. Finally, he requested their release. Mayor Liu, believing that the real perpetrator had escaped and that there was no need to detain the suspects for long, telegraphed Chief Chen at 8:00 AM on the 15th to release them and to vigorously pursue the real perpetrator. (June 16th)

Central Army Blockades Bozhou 56

Sun Dianying Asks Lu Zhonglin for Relief

Bengbu Dispatch: The Central Army's Wang Jun division has been besieging Bozhou for over a month. Sun Dianying had built three strong lines of moats and densely laid obstacles outside Bozhou, which were all broken through by the Central Army. Now, Sun's troops are relying on the defenses within the city to hold out desperately. The Central Army, wishing to completely annihilate Sun's forces but also considering that Bozhou is a prosperous area in northern Anhui, is reluctant to use heavy artillery to bombard it, so it is strictly blockading it to achieve a complete resolution. According to the Yun Ri Bao, Sun's show of sincerity to the Central Government is entirely a tactic to ease our side's vigilance so that he can seize the opportunity to seek aid from the Northwest. The General Headquarters' field headquarters has announced for days that it has intercepted many telegrams from Sun Dianying in Bozhou seeking aid from Feng Yuxiang, Yan Xishan, Lu Zhonglin, and Sun Liangcheng. The following two excerpts can show that he has reached a state of desperation: (1) Sun Dianying's telegram to Lu Zhonglin in Zhengzhou stated: "My troops have been besieged for over a month, and our supplies of food and ammunition have long been exhausted. Since the 20th of last month, I have ordered the troops to seize the new wheat within our defense area to勉資維持 (勉資維持). Now, the new wheat is also depleted, and the enemy's siege is increasingly urgent. Our ammunition is exhausted, so I have ordered our troops to hold with white blades. Bozhou is in imminent danger. Please send a large force to reinforce us quickly and provide us with financial and ammunition assistance." (2) Sun Dianying's telegram to Sun Liangcheng stated: "General Commander Sun, Shao Yun, your distinguished seal. Since troops were drawn to aid Lucheng on the 6th, the enemy's 3rd Army, 7th Division has sent another brigade to besiege Bozhou, attacking fiercely day and night. I led the troops to charge three times but failed to break through. Last night's bloody battle was the fiercest. We have no more bullets for our guns and cannons. Although the officers and soldiers are brave, it is truly difficult to resist the enemy with bare hands. Ammunition transported from Qixian could not be delivered because Bozhou is in heavy encirclement and remains in Zhecheng. Bozhou's crisis is imminent. Even if we wanted to retreat, we cannot fly out of this heavy encirclement. Now the enemy is approaching the West Gate. If we lose it, we can only be slaughtered to repay your kindness. What else is there to say? If I fail in my duties, I earnestly request that you order a strong force to come to our aid day and night; otherwise, we will be waiting to die. My mind and strength are exhausted, and I cannot say all that I wish. Sun Kuiyuan bows respectfully (June 16th)."

Anhui Finance and Education Commissioners Arrive in Wuhu 57

Sun Shengwu's Talk on Anhui's Finances

Wuhu Dispatch: Anhui's Finance Commissioner Sun Shengwu recently stated that the province's financial situation has reached a critical point, with resources exhausted and coping becoming extremely difficult. Wuhu, being the financial center of Anhui, has long been considered a place to negotiate loans with the banking community. During his previous trip to Shanghai, he telegraphed the heads of the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications in Wuhu to go to Shanghai for preliminary talks. Now, with the end of the 18th accounting year approaching, all government expenses must be cleared and paid as a conclusion. Due to the urgent need for funds, he arrived in Wuhu yesterday (the 14th) from Anqing on the Anfeng military vessel for further talks. Upon arrival at the port, officials from various agencies welcomed him. He then lodged at the Bank of China. This morning, I paid him a visit and asked about the recent financial situation in Anhui. Mr. Sun's remarks were as follows: "Anhui's finances were originally very difficult, but not as dire as they are now. This is because the northern part of Anhui has suffered from war and banditry this year, resulting in no tax revenue. Although there is tax revenue in southern and central Anhui, the amount is meager and insufficient to cover expenses. The only item with relatively high revenue is salt tax, followed by wheat tax. As for rice levies, there is almost no tax revenue to speak of because there is no rice export, which is a huge loss. When I took office in May, the province's government and temporary expenses owed totaled over 800,000 yuan. After repeated efforts, I managed to allocate 600,000 yuan, but there is still an outstanding debt of over 200,000 yuan. The province's finances are almost in a state of collapse. After reorganization, things began to show some progress. There are over 400 cases of county magistrates owing public funds, amounting to a substantial sum. We are now drafting ten measures to reorganize the collection of funds by county magistrates, which will be submitted to the provincial government for deliberation and implementation this Tuesday. The time limit for the allocation of funds to various counties is also strictly set. Those who fail to collect 40% to 50% of the allocated funds will be given demerits or dismissed. Currently, the province's monthly revenue is only over 400,000 yuan. Regarding the outstanding debts from the old budget, we will definitely clear them by the end of this fiscal year so that the new budget for the 19th year can begin, ensuring that Anhui's finances do not encounter difficulties again. My visit here is for this matter and to have talks with the banking community in Wuhu. I plan to return to the province tonight, or I may need to make a trip to Beijing temporarily."

Education Commissioner Cheng Tianfang previously went to northern Anhui for inspection and was scheduled to arrive in Wuhu from Beijing the day before yesterday afternoon. Officials from various agencies here waited at the riverfront to welcome him, but he did not arrive after the scheduled time. Everyone assumed that he had gone directly back to Anqing and did not disembark in Wuhu, so they all dispersed and returned home. Unexpectedly, Mr. Cheng arrived in the port from Beijing in the evening and disembarked, lodging at the Zhonghua Hotel by the river. The next morning, various sectors learned the news that Cheng had gone with Provincial Inspector Wang Dexi to inspect Provincial No. 7 Middle School, No. 2 Vocational School for Girls, and other schools. At 1:00 PM, the Education Funding Management Office, the Popular Education Center, and various middle schools held a welcome meeting at the Opera Stage, attended by over a thousand people. The chairman, Principal Ke Defa of No. 7 Middle School, delivered a welcoming speech, saying that since Commissioner Cheng came to Anhui, the province's education funding has increased by 300,000 yuan, and three more middle schools have been established, which is truly worth welcoming. Then Mr. Cheng took the stage to give a speech, briefly saying that there are several things he wants to tell the students today. The province's population totals 30 million, but there are only over 20 middle schools, with fewer than 10,000 students. This means that on average, only one person out of 3,000 receives middle school education. You must know that those who should bear major responsibilities for the country and society are not the uneducated people, nor are they the small number of university students who have received specialized education; they are entirely dependent on middle school students. China's international status is extremely dangerous. Political aggression is already alarming, and economic aggression is even more painful. For example, in the past, industrial and commercial goods mostly relied on foreign countries, but in recent years, even agricultural products such as rice and wheat, which are needed for people's food, are all seeking help from foreigners. The danger of national extinction and racial annihilation is imminent. The biggest common ills of the Chinese people are two: one is laziness, only thinking of enjoying the fruits of others' labor and unwilling to work hard; the other is disunity, unwilling to cooperate wholeheartedly and only knowing how to undermine each other. I deeply hope that we can get rid of these bad habits, work hard, and bear major responsibilities for the country and society. After the meeting, Mr. Cheng took the Jiang'an ship back to the province (the 15th).

Liu and Lu Still Locked in Stalemate in Fuzhou 58

Contact Also Made on Yongtai Side

Fuzhou Maintained by Marine Corps

Fuzhou Dispatch: The Liu He Ding and Lu Xingbang divisions engaged in battle in the northwestern suburbs of Fuzhou. At 10:00 PM on the 9th, the Lu division's Qian Yu Guang and Chen Rong Biao regiments again engaged in fierce fighting with the Liu division's Jiang Yan and Yan Xi Min regiments at Ling Tou on the northern route and Wen Shan on the western route. The artillery fire was even heavier than on the 7th and 8th. By 6:00 AM on the 10th, the Lu division had suffered heavy casualties due to the Liu division's artillery bombardment. The Qian regiment, which was responsible for the northern route, completely collapsed, and regimental commander Qian Yu Guang disappeared (or it was rumored that he was shot by brigade commander Lu Xing Rong). The Chen regiment, which was responsible for the western route, also suffered heavy casualties, with one battalion commander captured and one battalion commander also retreating. The Liu division then cleared the battlefield on the 10th morning and afternoon and exchanged the troops in the front and rear to rest. From 10:00 PM on the 10th, the two sides again engaged in battle at Xiang Ling Creek on the northern route and Miao Feng Wen Shan on the western route. Because it was farther from the city, no gunfire was heard in the city. However, because the Lu division had been repeatedly defeated on the northwestern routes, it specially transferred over a thousand troops from Sun Guo Zhen's division's supplementary team, intending to invade Fuzhou's southern route from Yongtai County. From the morning of the 11th, they had already engaged in battle with the rear team of Chen Wan Tai's brigade of the Liu division. According to the Liu division's battle report, the enemy suffered over 1,000 casualties and abandoned over 800 rifles. The Second Brigade, which had been specially transferred and reorganized from the province's defense forces, led by brigade commander Lu Xin Ming, was dispatched from Yan Ping to the western countryside of Min Hou to join Lu Xing Rong and the two independent regiments of Chen Rong Biao and Wang Tian Rui. The Liu division also added Chen Wan Tai's brigade to the front line to join the two brigades of Gui Zhen Yuan and Liu Shang Zhi. It is estimated that the front-line troops of both sides numbered over 20,000. As for the defense of the rear in Fuzhou, it is now being maintained by the Marine Corps. The Third Regiment of the 22nd Brigade of the Marine Corps, led by Lin Bing Zhou, entered the city from Nantai Xiadu yesterday and is stationed at the former site of the Army Primary School in front of the Governor's Office. It is also heard that the Central Government may send two airplanes to Fujian within days to assist in the battle, and the South Parade Ground has been designated as the airfield (June 11th).

Another Dispatch: Lu He Ding specially transferred Chen's Brigade and its various regiments stationed in Quanzhou back to the province to support the defense. The brigade arrived yesterday (the 13th) at noon on eight ships, including the Zhenbo, and twelve洋駁 (洋駁), and was assigned to the front line that evening, changing from defense to offense. The previous battle news was slightly more intense from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM yesterday morning and from 2:00 AM to 4:00 AM today. According to investigations, yesterday morning, the Liu division's troops attacked the Lu side's position from Tong Pan Shan, the northern gate, and engaged in hand-to-hand combat with the Lu troops several times, occupying the position of the Shrine of Soldiers Killed in Action from the Li Hou Ji era. The Lu Xing Rong troops have retreated to Baisha, but the two sides are still in a stalemate. As for those in the provincial agencies who are related to the enemy, they have been severely investigated and arrested in recent days. For example, the Second Division's liaison office in the province, the dare-to-be detective's office, the Zhonghe Pharmacy in the city, and Deng's residence in Fushi Lane were sealed off and inspected. This afternoon, a Lu division scout named Chen Qing and others were temporarily arrested. However, this battle has lasted for a week, and the merchants and residents of the Fuzhou walls and the villages along the northwestern battle lines are all complaining endlessly. Therefore, rumors of naval mediation are rampant, and the people also have this hope so that they can be spared from the scourge of war as soon as possible (June 14th).

Zhejiang Province Implements Reduction of Silk Levy 59

Levy Rate Reduced by One Quarter

The Zhejiang Provincial Government, in order to fundamentally remedy the declining silk industry in Zhejiang, has resolved two measures: (1) To encourage the use of machines to weave silk, the product will be completely tax-free. (2) The silk levy rate will be reduced by one quarter. The first measure of encouraging machine-woven silk has already been communicated to various counties for compliance. The second measure was delayed until yesterday due to the complicated procedures involved in tax revenue. It was communicated to various统捐局 (统捐局) for compliance, to be implemented from June 16th of the 19th year. All silk levy rates will be reduced by one quarter based on the original levy rates. The original annual payment of 400,000 yuan for silk levies collected by the Hangzhou Guancheng Hall and the silk levy office will also be reduced by one quarter from the 16th, totaling an annual amount of 300,000 yuan. However, the levy on rayon will be appropriately increased because the import of this item has increased sharply in recent years. After several negotiations between the Finance Department and the rayon levy office, it was decided to increase the original amount of 140,000 yuan by 10%, totaling an annual payment of 155,000 yuan.

Guangdong Province

Progress of Reorganization of Merchant Groups 61

Provincial Party Department Agrees to New Businessmen's Association's Demands

Guidance Committee Members All Elected

Guangzhou Dispatch: The Guangdong Provincial Party Department, in order to unify the businessmen's movement throughout the province, revoked the All-Province Businessmen's Association Reorganization Committee previously appointed to form an organization. It re-established methods for the organization of the Guangdong All-Province Businessmen's Organization Guidance Committee. The regulations stipulated that the committee would have nine members, with the old and new businessmen's associations each recommending three members from the thirteen people who attended the previous meeting, and the Party Department would add three members from the former Provincial Businessmen's Association to jointly form the committee. The old businessmen's association had already elected Liu Yin Xun, Chen Zan Chen, and Zhou Run Zhi. However, the new businessmen's association did not have enough members to meet the legal requirements, and they believed that the organization method of the Party Department adding three members from the former Provincial Businessmen's Association was not in accordance with the requirements. The Provincial Party Department's Training Department changed the proposal to have the Party Department appoint three members to avoid setting a precedent for the reorganization of business associations in various counties in the future. At that time, the Provincial Training Department did not express any opinions, which led to the new businessmen's association firmly opposing the election of committee members, causing twists and turns. On the morning of the 11th, the Provincial Training Department again urged the new businessmen's association members to go to the Party Department to elect three attending committee members. Liang Yucai and others then reiterated their reasons, requesting that the proposal of the Party Department adding three members from the Provincial Businessmen's Association be revoked and changed to the Party Department appointing three members instead of using the name of the Provincial Businessmen's Association, which had already been dissolved, before they would agree to the election. The attitude was extremely resolute. At that time, the Provincial Party Department Executive Committee was holding a meeting, and the Secretary of the Provincial Training Department, Lin, reported the matter to the Director of the Training Department, Chen Mingshu. Chen then explained to the new businessmen's association members that the Party Department was well aware of the content of the province's businessmen's groups and would never take sides. As for the addition of the three members from the former Provincial Businessmen's Association causing disputes, it could also be changed to accept the new businessmen's association's opinion of having the Party Department appoint three members instead of using the name of the Provincial Businessmen's Association. After listening, the seven members of the new businessmen's association, Hu Song Tang, Peng Chu Li, Liang Yu Cai, Zhi Zi Qing, Liang Jing Yun, Zhang Song Xian, and Liu Wei Wen, felt satisfied and, as the number of people had exceeded half of the thirteen, they immediately elected Zou Dian Bang, Peng Chu Li, and Liang Yu Cai as the result. Subsequently, the Provincial Party Department also appointed Cheng Shao Jie, Pan Qi Yuan, and Huo Jiong Tang to join the Liu Yin Xun, Chen Zan Chen, and Zhou Run Zhi, who had already been elected by the old businessmen's association, totaling nine people. At this point, the members of the Guangdong All-Province Businessmen's Organization Guidance Committee were all elected. Once a meeting is convened, they will immediately elect officers and draft regulations and take over the old and new business associations to intensify their work (the 12th).

The Zheng犯 (郑犯) in the Mu Bin Extortion Case is Apprehended: In the case of the former Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Mu Bin, being extorted by bandits, the police detectives of the Public Security Bureau successively arrested the main criminals in the case, Hang Bing Kui and Lu Xue Li. Zhenjiang 66

Security Office Examines Officials: The Jiangsu Provincial Security Office previously established the First and Second Regiments in order to expand its strength. The Coal Industry Labor-Capital Dispute is Resolved: The Zhenjiang Coal and Iron Industry找夫 (找夫) Trade Union previously requested the capitalists to increase wages due to the rising cost of living, and the dispute was not resolved. Yesterday, the Gongzheng Association held a second mediation meeting and resolved the following: (1) In addition to the original wages, twelve copper coins per ton will be added for rice subsidies. (2) The rice subsidy added this time will be cancelled by half when the rice returns to 15 yuan, and completely cancelled when the rice returns to 13 yuan. (3) The working hours set by the labor side will end at 6:00 PM, but if there is still more than six tons of cargo that has been loaded and not completed, the labor side should load it all, and no price increase is allowed. (4) The labor side must not increase the 300 copper coins per ton charged to cargo ships for other reasons. After the discussion, the representatives of both parties signed the agreement, and the coal industry turmoil came to an end.

Important News

Japan Decides to Revitalize Family Education 73

Ten Concrete Measures

Tokyo News Agency of the World News Society: The Family Education Study and Discussion Council, initiated by the Japanese Ministry of Education, held a special meeting on the 9th regarding family education. After discussing the proposals put forward by representatives of women's education from various prefectures and counties, it was decided to implement ten concrete measures to promote family education, as follows:

(1) For the general adult population, especially mothers, to study methods for cultivating knowledge about family education matters. (2) To expect the completion of childcare facilities outside of schools. (3) To seek improvement of youth cultivation and entertainment facilities. (4) To provide teachers and instructors with research methods regarding family education matters. (5) To make the connection between family and school more complete. (6) To seek improvement and revitalization of child protection endeavors. (7) To promote a general trend of improvement regarding family education. (8) To eliminate obstacles to the revitalization of family education. (9) To guide prefectures, counties, and villages to seek facilities for improving family education and to provide appropriate assistance for appropriate facilities. (10) The Ministry of Education issues instructions and encouragement for the improvement and revitalization of family education and promotes the popularization of facilities.

American University

Establishes Department of Chinese Studies 74

Appoints Jiang Kanghu as Department Head

Since the Great War, educators in various European and American countries with a global perspective have been interested in bridging Eastern and Western cultures to create a basis for world harmony. Therefore, they have collected Chinese classics without reservation. For example, the Library of Congress in Washington, D.C., and the library of McGill University (transliteration) in Canada each hold more than 100,000 volumes of Chinese books and continue to add to them without slackening. Their attention to our country's culture can be imagined. According to a recent report in the San Francisco Times, McGill University in Montreal, Canada, has decided to establish a Department of Chinese Studies starting this autumn and has appointed Dr. Jiang Kanghu of our country as the department head and chief lecturer. At the same time, Collie University has specially invited Mr. Jiang to teach Eastern philosophy and art. This is truly the beginning of the practical integration of Eastern and Western cultures and will have a positive impact on our country's international standing.

Important Issues Concerning Libraries 75

Ministry of Education's Instructions to the China Library Association

The Ministry of Education previously received a report from the China Library Association based on the resolutions of the first annual meeting, requesting adoption. The Ministry of Education recently replied to the association, stating that the report and proposals were noted and that some of the points were worthy of adoption. The replies are as follows: (1) "Regarding the promulgation of laws and regulations for establishing library standards": The library regulations were promulgated on May 10. As for the establishment standards, the Ministry is currently conducting a survey of the situation of libraries nationwide and plans to solicit opinions from library experts before compiling them. (2) "Regarding increasing library funding": The funds for social education should be temporarily set at 10% to 20% of the total education funding. This was previously approved by the former University Council and reported to the National Government, and orders were issued to comply with it. However, the scope of social education is very broad, and libraries are one of the social education endeavors. It is difficult to use all the social education funds exclusively for this one endeavor. Therefore, the proportion of direct funding will be temporarily postponed to allow for flexibility. As for the book purchasing expenses for schools at all levels, orders should be issued to pay special attention to it and determine it appropriately. (3) "Regarding encouraging the establishment of libraries": The Second National Education Conference resolved to prepare for the establishment of a central library within eighteen years. The Ministry is currently planning to carry it out. Before the central library is established, a library department will be established within the Central Education Center this year to collect and display Chinese and foreign books related to education. As for various specialized and general public and children's libraries, the Ministry plans to order the education departments of various provinces and the education bureaus of various special municipalities to actively increase their establishment starting this year. (4) "Regarding the need for experts to guide the development of library services": Permission is granted to instruct the education departments of various provinces and the education bureaus of various special municipalities to handle this matter appropriately. (5) "Regarding the importance of specialized library personnel": (1) The establishment of specialized library schools should be temporarily postponed. Subsidies for already established library schools should be handled in accordance with the regulations for private schools. (2) Permission is granted to instruct universities to add library science courses or library science departments to their faculties of arts or education. (3) Permission is granted to instruct the education departments of various provinces, the education bureaus of various special municipalities, and Tsinghua University to appropriately determine the number of library science students to be sent abroad each year. (4) The Ministry's interim standards for primary and secondary school curricula are currently being tested. When they are revised in the future, library science can be appropriately added. Guidance on the use of systematic books and publications in schools at all levels is temporarily not required to be specified by the Ministry. (6) "Regarding the implementation of the resolutions of the First National Education Conference": The former University Council has already selected and issued orders to comply with the main points. (7) "Regarding the implementation of the Publishing Law": The formulation of copyright and publishing laws falls under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of the Interior. The regulations for submitting newly published books promulgated by the former University Council have now been revised by the Ministry. The regulations for submitting books by various bookstores stipulate that each bookstore must submit four copies of newly published books to the provincial education department or special municipal education bureau where the publisher is located. One copy will be kept by the provincial or municipal education administrative agency, and the remaining three copies will be forwarded to the Ministry for distribution to the Ministry's library, the Central Education Center, and the Central Library. Requiring more copies to be submitted is clearly inconsistent with the provisions of the case and cannot be followed. Furthermore, although the National Romanization has been promulgated, it is only the second method for promoting the national language and can be used by scholars for reference and research. Its promotion has not yet become widespread, and it is not appropriate to force its immediate implementation. (8) "Regarding reducing the price of educational books and newspapers": Permission is granted for the Ministry to instruct various educational institutions to comply with this. (9) "Regarding rewarding those who wholeheartedly engage in library work": "Permission is granted to handle this in accordance with the regulations on donating funds to establish schools." (10) "Regarding stipulating independent administrative control of school libraries": Due to many practical difficulties, there is no need to discuss this. (11) "Regarding the transfer of the official book bureaus of various provinces to the management of provincial libraries": The situations of the official book bureaus in various provinces are different. If it is necessary and possible to merge the official book bureaus in various provinces and regions, a request should be submitted to the competent authorities of the province for investigation and approval. (12) "Regarding the stipulation to hold a Library Movement Week": This can be promoted incidentally during literacy campaigns or public education lectures in various provinces or special municipalities, without holding it separately. Please take note of the above points separately.

As the vacation was about to end, the provincial government repeatedly telegraphed him to return. New Budget for Anhui Education Funds Determined 77

Totaling 2.07 Million Yuan

An Increase of 370,000 Yuan Compared to the Previous Year

The new budget (for the 19th year) for Anhui Province's education funds has been compiled and is currently awaiting review by the provincial government. The total amount of this budget is 2.07 million yuan, an increase of 370,000 yuan compared to the previous year. This is because one new middle school (Chuxian Middle School), three vernacular education halls (one each in Datong, Tunxi, and Zhengyang), one public sports field (converted from the Huazhong venue), and one rural normal school (converted from the private rural normal school in Bengbu) should be added this year, requiring a total of 80,000 yuan for establishment and recurring expenses. The cost of studying abroad has increased significantly due to changes in the price of gold and increased subsidies for domestic universities, totaling more than 40,000 yuan. In addition, the number of classes in the original primary and secondary schools has increased, the food expenses for normal school students have increased (from 5 yuan per person to 6 yuan), and the labor and food expenses for servants and workers have increased (from 8 yuan per person to 9 yuan). Therefore, the increase is as described above and will be reviewed by the provincial government.

Zhejiang University College of Agriculture

Affiliated Provincial Senior High School Agricultural Science Department 79

In order to cultivate agricultural science professionals, the Zhejiang Education Department plans to establish a senior agricultural science high school affiliated with the Zhejiang University College of Agriculture. It has been agreed with the College of Agriculture. It is reported that the affiliated department this year will be the first grade of senior high school agricultural science. This grade is divided into three departments: agronomy, forestry, and agricultural society. Each department will recruit 25 new students. The length of study is three years. Qualifications for application include graduation from junior high school and possession of a certificate of completion equivalent to junior high school graduation. The examination subjects, in addition to physical examination and oral examination, are the Three People's Principles, Chinese language, English language, mathematics (algebra and geometry), physics, chemistry, and biology. Registration will be from October 10 to October 25. The examination will begin on October 26. After being admitted, new students must bring a guarantee, a letter of intent, and a receipt from the bank designated by the College of Agriculture for payment of fees to the college before September 10 to receive their admission certificate and formally enroll. Those who wish to inquire about recruitment matters or request a prospectus can send a letter with a detailed address and four cents of postage to Zhejiang University, Putang Lane, Hangzhou, and they will receive a reply.

Farm Education Hall Clinic Enthusiastically Provides Relief 80

It was discovered that a large gang of bandits had appeared in the area of Zhouwang Mountain near Tangshan, Nanjing. The villages of Dongguo Sai Xixiang and others were burned. Upon hearing the news, the Tangshan Club telegraphed Nanjing to transfer the National Government Guard Regiment to encircle and suppress them. However, there were no less than one hundred bandits, fully equipped with guns, machinery and horses. The officers and soldiers numbered only seventy. They launched a fierce frontal attack and held out until noon on the 13th, when the bandits finally retreated. One bandit was beheaded and his head displayed in front of the club. Among the officers and soldiers, one was seriously injured and died before he could be rescued, three were seriously injured, and more than ten were slightly injured. All were treated by the clinic of the Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Education Hall. Director Chen of the clinic personally went to Nanjing to transfer an ambulance from the Central Hospital to send the seriously injured to Nanjing for treatment. Although the hall was busy providing relief, the work of the various departments continued as usual. It is also reported that the headquarters has successively transferred more than a dozen vehicles of soldiers to pursue the remaining bandits.

Capital Prepares to Establish Water Conservancy College 81

Since the resolutions of the Second Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee established agricultural policy as the foundation for the development of industry and commerce, the national water conservancy undertaking has gradually developed. There is a shortage of specialized water conservancy personnel. At the recent plenary session of the Construction Committee, Vice Chairman Zeng Yangfu proposed that the committee, in consultation with the Ministry of Education, establish a water conservancy vocational college in the capital to train water conservancy technical personnel to meet the needs, and that a water conservancy test field be attached to it. It is estimated that a total of approximately 200,000 yuan is needed for establishment expenses and approximately 240,000 yuan for annual recurring expenses. It is proposed that a portion of the recurring expenses be discussed and allocated by the committee in consultation with the relevant provinces, and that the remaining portion and the establishment expenses be requested by the committee to the Executive Yuan to order the Ministry of Finance to allocate funds. The proposal was discussed and resolved at the conference to consult with the Ministry of Education before jointly submitting a request to the Executive Yuan to order the Ministry of Finance to allocate funds so that it could be established as soon as possible.

Work of the Ministry of Education on Mongolian and Tibetan Education 82

Since its establishment several months ago, the Mongolian and Tibetan Education Department of the Ministry of Education has been working actively. The Ministry of Education submitted a summary report to the Central Government on the actual work of the department from November of the eighteenth year to May of this year. The key points of the report are extracted below: (1) "Implementation of the Resolutions of the Second Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee on Mongolian and Tibetan Education": Establishment of the Mongolian and Tibetan Education Department (divided into two sections: (1) on Mongolian education; (2) on Tibetan education; currently, only one section is established to handle both Mongolian and Tibetan education); Preparation for the Nanjing and Kangding Mongolian and Tibetan Schools (the organizational outlines of the two schools have been revised and sent to the Executive Yuan for approval); Establishment of the Tibetan Children's Tutoring School in Beijing (established in February of this year, with expenses paid by the national treasury). (2) "Investigation of Mongolian and Tibetan Education": Formulation of investigation forms (divided into two types: secondary education, primary education, and private school investigation forms, with a total of 100 copies issued); Statistics on schools (approximately 50 Mongolian and Tibetan universities, middle schools, and primary schools in total). (3) "Broadcast of the Mongolian and Tibetan Education Program and its Implementation Plan": Key points of the Mongolian and Tibetan Education Implementation Program (formulated in March of this year and approved by the Central Government); Mongolian and Tibetan Education Implementation Plan (revised and approved by the Second National Education Conference in April of this year). (4) "Opening of the Mongolian and Tibetan Classes at the Central Political School and the Central University of Peiping": The Mongolian and Tibetan Class at the Central Political School was established in the spring of this year. The Mongolian and Tibetan Classes at Peiping and Central University are approved to be established during the summer vacation of this year. (5) "Translation of the Educational Purpose of the Republic of China and Various Laws and Regulations of the Ministry and Distribution to Various Mongolian and Tibetan Regions": The Educational Purpose of the Republic of China and its Implementation Guidelines (translated in December of last year); Revised Organizational Law of the Ministry of Education (January of this year); Regulations of the Educational Association (February); Regulations on the Treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan Students, National Sports Law, and Mongolian and Tibetan Education Implementation Program (all in March); Regulations on Private Schools (April). (6) "Collection of Mongolian and Tibetan Books": Books such as the Trilingual San Min Chu I, Trilingual Handbook, etc., were sent by the Peiping Library, totaling 49 volumes. Books such as the Explanations of the History of the Liao, Jin, and Yuan Dynasties, etc., were first sent by the Archives Preservation Office of the Ministry of Education in Peiping, totaling 71 volumes, for a total of 120 volumes.

Sports

My Opinion on the Failure of the Chinese Basketball Team (Member Lu Zhongen) 94

I am one of the members of the Chinese basketball team that attended the Far Eastern Games. I should not have any discussion about the entire team, but since Mr. Xu's commentary was published in this column on Sunday, I cannot bear not to briefly share my humble opinions with the readers for a study.

The players representing our country this time are all first-class talents. Therefore, the people of the country have a 12-point belief in this year's team. Victory is not worth mentioning. How can one know that there are unexpected things in the world? Unemotional news came, turning the championship that the public thought we had into a castle in the air. Depressed and frustrated, there is no end to it. However, my concept is the opposite of the public. Before departure, I repeatedly discussed with friends the possible dangers of this year's championship. The main points that I expected are listed below:

Intellectual Aspects 95

(1) In terms of individual temperament, our team members generally lack self-restraint. Each person's character seems too fervent. Every time they step onto the field, they inevitably become overly eager to win and lose control of themselves. There are two main reasons for this: first, a lack of experience; second, the overwhelming cheers of our countrymen cause a sense of bewilderment among the young players. They feel nervous and anxious. During the first match against Japan, I observed from the sidelines that after our players got the ball, they seemed at a loss, unsure whether to advance, retreat, shoot, or pass. They either failed to act when they should have, or acted inappropriately, resulting in no success.

Technical Aspects 96

(1) During regular practice, there is insufficient preparation in both offense and defense. The only offensive tactics emphasized are the center jump and out-of-bounds plays from the defensive area. There is no practice for out-of-bounds plays on the sidelines, rebounding under the basket, or offensive plays during free throws. In defense, only one tactic is emphasized: the five-man revolve system. From what I've seen in basketball games, there are six types of offensive and defensive strategies (I won't go into detail now, but I can discuss them further when I have time). Within these six types, each team should have at least two: one for dealing with brave and reckless teams, and another for dealing with agile and skillful teams. The Philippines team is like Shanghai’s Hujiang and Xiqing, always setting traps. If our team only has one tactic, the chances of winning a complete victory are slim. The first and second matches should not use the same strategy, because the opponent will be prepared for the second match. A ball game is like a battle: the best strategy is to attack when the enemy is unprepared. Japan is certainly brave, but if China can outsmart them (like the Philippines did against Japan), victory will not be difficult. As for the Philippines, our Chinese team has a very good chance of winning. Unfortunately, bad luck and unexpected changes led to defeat. These points are sufficient to prove that my predictions for this championship were not unfounded, but the extent of our defeats in each match was beyond my expectations.

Four Matches 97

The lineup for the first match against Japan was: Tang Baokun, Yao Enhan, Liu Jianchang, Li Guochen, and Wang Xiliang. After the start, the Japanese team quickly scored six points, causing confusion in the Chinese team. We could only parry but not counterattack. It wasn't until the last ten minutes when Wei Pengyun replaced Yao Enhan that the team showed any improvement. With three minutes remaining, the coach replaced Wang Xiliang with me (which wasn't necessary). After entering the game, I seized a good opportunity to score a basket from under the hoop. The whistle blew and the buzzer sounded. China lost to Japan by fifteen points (a new Far Eastern record). In this match, our two forwards, Liu and Yao, did not perform well, and the players' movements were very sluggish. The Japanese team, on the other hand, were incredibly brave, with their two forwards scoring more than thirty points. With such effective offense and defense, it's no wonder we suffered a defeat.

The lineup for the second match against the Philippines was: Tang Baokun, Yao Enhan, Liu Jianchang, Li Guochen, and me. Our team showed much more progress compared to the first match. Unfortunately, Tang was closely guarded and had no scoring opportunities during his three free throws. If Tang could have played to his strengths, our team's victory would have been predictable.

The lineup for the third match against Japan was: Tang Baokun, Wei Pengyun, Liu Jianchang, Li Guochen, and me. According to the coach's instructions, we used a man-to-man defense. Unfortunately, we had no practice with this strategy, so it was disorganized. After ten minutes, Wang Xiliang replaced me. By the end of the first half, we were down by ten points. In the second half, the lineup was changed again, with Chen Chenkui, Yao Enhan, Wang Yuzeng, and Liu Guanjun joining me. After the start, our team played very bravely, with Chen, Yao, and Wang each scoring a basket. The Japanese team then called a timeout. After the restart, the Japanese scored two more baskets, and our team called a timeout. While we were discussing strategy, the coach suddenly replaced the entire lineup. At this point, there were still ten minutes left in the game, and there was hope for a comeback. Who knew that after this substitution, we would collapse completely and lose to the Japanese by another seventeen points. What a tragedy!

The lineup for the fourth match against the Philippines was: Tang Baokun, Chen Shengkui, Wang Yuzeng, Liu Guanjun, and me. As soon as the whistle blew, the two sides engaged in a fierce contest. Our team fought desperately, and the score was ten to two in our favor. When the score reached twenty to nine, Li Guochen replaced me, Yao Enhan replaced Chen, and Liu Jianchang replaced Wang. By the end of the first half, our team was ahead by thirty to fifteen. After the start of the second half, the Philippines team suddenly displayed their ultimate skills and launched a strong attack. The score gradually narrowed. With only five points separating the teams, I re-entered the game and Liu Guanjun left. Our team's momentum picked up again, with Li, Liu, and I each scoring a basket. The crowd cheered. Our team's performance was excellent, and we were evenly matched with the Philippines. But disaster struck from the sky! Xing suddenly fouled for the fourth time and was disqualified. Liu re-entered the game. After this substitution, our team's morale suddenly collapsed, and the Philippines team launched a fierce counterattack. As a result, our team lost to the Philippines by four points, resulting in four losses in four matches.

Overview 98

The reason for these defeats was not due to a lack of technical skill, but rather a lack of essential basketball knowledge. In addition to what I've mentioned, there are a couple of other points worth noting:

(1) The discipline of our basketball team members was unmatched by other teams. Apart from attending meetings, everyone rested in the dormitory all day and never stepped out of line. As a result, the players were constantly thinking about the games. They regarded basketball as more important than their own lives, which led to bewilderment and confusion when they got the ball during the matches.

(2) In each match, there was no one to command the team's movements and serve as the team's leader (the same problem as the soccer team this year). As a result, when one person panicked, the entire team was thrown into chaos, leading to an unrecoverable disaster.

What About the Referees? 99

Various newspapers have offered very detailed commentary on the referees. But from my perspective, the referees in this competition had absolutely no experience in officiating, and they were also unfamiliar with the rules. I recall that during the first match, I discussed the new rules with them (such as the regulations for jump balls and free throws) for about two minutes, and they had no answers. As a result, the referee's inappropriate rulings sparked discontent among the spectators. Of course, the referees have a close relationship with the competition, but in light of the results of this competition, our team's defeat cannot be entirely blamed on the referees. If our team could have calmly faced Japan and the Philippines with our inherent abilities, I can confidently say that victory would have been within our grasp. Look at the Philippines' victory over Japan. Were the referees any less incompetent? Yet, the Philippines team maintained their composure throughout, outmaneuvering their opponents with ingenuity and winning the championship. In conclusion, based on the standard of the previous matches, the Philippines team was the best and the Chinese team was the worst. But from my perspective, if our team could have all played to their strengths and remained calm, the championship would have been ours.

Well, there's no point in dwelling on the past. The next tournament is four years away. I hope that our countrymen who are passionate about sports can promote and encourage them tirelessly and impartially. Everyone should have the spirit of drawing their swords and fighting bravely, so that we can wash away the shame of this year in the next tournament. I will discuss how to promote and encourage this when I have time. Before departing, I had intended to publish the training process and the possibilities and impossibilities of winning the championship in the newspapers, but I was afraid of causing misunderstandings, so I dared not try.

A One-Point Difference in the Basketball Game

Girls Beat Boys 101

Liangjiang No. 27 News, No. 26

Yesterday (the 17th) at 4 p.m., the Liangjiang Women's Basketball Team, at the invitation of the News Team, competed at the China Basketball Hall. They used men's rules. The News Team is composed of people from the local news and sports circles, and their strength is exceptionally strong. But since the Liangjiang team has been practicing men's rules, their progress in basketball skills has been significant. It can be seen from their victory yesterday. As soon as the whistle blew, both sides started chasing after each other. In less than a minute, Liangjiang's Zhuang Shuyu scored the first point, followed by Shao Jinying with another, making it 4-0, taking the lead. Seeing the fierce attack, the News Team fought back hard, and Pei Xiyuan, Zhuang Huaiqing and others scored successively. At the end of the first quarter, the News Team was ahead with 6-4. In the second quarter, Liangjiang tried to recover, and the defense gradually became more stable, while the forwards were exceptionally agile. Shao Jinying and Xi Jun scored points one after another, and the score increased steadily. At the end of the first half, Liangjiang turned the tables and won with 18-14. At the beginning of the second half, the two teams were close in score, so the competition was even more intense. The News Team was gradually running out of stamina, while the Liangjiang team was more flexible. So at the end of the third quarter, Liangjiang won again with 24-18. At the beginning of the fourth quarter, the News Team was in a bad situation and had to try hard to save the situation, so the competition was unprecedentedly fierce. In the News Team, Lu Xiangqian ran the entire court and was the most outstanding player. As expected, the score gradually caught up, becoming a tie at 26. At this time, the score was equal, and both teams were in a critical situation, making the audience restless. Then, the News Team was penalized for a foul, and Liangjiang scored a point. Before the timekeeper announced the end, Liangjiang won with 27-26 and returned in triumph.

Special Report

Random Notes on Studying Japanese Education (3) 104

(Hu Shuyi)

In Tokyo, in addition to the Municipal Education Bureau, there is the Tokyo Prefectural Education Department. After our visit, we felt that the organization and uniformity and practicality were the strengths of Japanese educational administration; however, it seemed to pay relatively little attention to research and guidance. In our discussions of educational systems, we learned that Japan's secondary education section is extremely complex, with seven-year-system high schools, middle schools, higher girls' schools, higher primary schools, normal schools, vocational schools, and vocational supplementary schools all distinct. As for normal school education, it has an independent system. Normal schools require graduation from higher elementary school and then entry into higher normal schools above vocational schools, their status on par with universities. This is the biggest difference from our country's school system. Perhaps the spirit of Japanese education lies in this point. On the afternoon of the 20th, at 1:00 PM, we went to the municipal Hisamatsu Normal Elementary School for a tour. The school is located in Hisamatsu-cho, Nihonbashi Ward, Tokyo. The school was founded in Meiji 6. It was rebuilt after the Tokyo Great Earthquake into a modern Western-style building made of steel and reinforced concrete. The cost of the building and equipment totaled 530,000 yen. Its perfection in architecture and equipment cannot be compared even with our country’s universities. We heard that the Tokyo City Government plans to build all elementary schools in the future in this style, showing their emphasis on elementary education. We were very impressed. After talking with the principal, we learned that the school grounds are about 60,175 square feet, with 1,250 students and 28 teachers. The highest salary is 180 yen per month, and the lowest is 55 yen. The total annual expenditure is more than 35,000 yen. In addition to educational administrative organs, school development matters are helped by the alumni association and the family support association, and the latter's enthusiasm for education is particularly admirable. They often donate to the school for economic construction, so the school's undertakings are thriving. Looking back at our country's schools at all levels, there are many families who do not interact with the school, let alone others. On May 21st, we visited the Tokyo School for the Deaf. The principal told us that the school was founded in Meiji 8. The teaching method initially used the finger-spelling method, but recently adopted the face-shape and mouth-shape teaching method, that is, pronunciation teaching, which is more effective. There are currently 122 students and 45 teachers. Most of the students are boarders and do not pay tuition. There are also normal school classes and research classes as teacher training institutions for deaf schools. As for the student graduation exit problem, we learned that the school has vocational subjects such as woodworking and various crafts, as well as tailoring, painting, and other skills. Being literate and having vocational skills means that those who would have been useless have, through the school's cultivation, become useful talents to society. The method is excellent. The teachers then led us to visit the school's various facilities and teaching methods, all of which were worthwhile. The students' handicrafts were exquisite and lovely, and there were also electric motors available for students to use in metalworking and woodworking. We heard that this school is a famous special education school in Tokyo. In the afternoon, we visited the private Takimien Girls' School. After talking with the principal for a week, we learned that the school is representative of the old-fashioned girls' schools in Tokyo. Its educational purpose is limited to literacy and further education. There are more than 800 students and more than 30 teachers. The annual cost is about 50,000 yen. After graduation, most of them go to women's universities. Teacher salaries range from 60 to 200 yen. The school buildings are not very spacious, but they are clean and tidy. The students are simple and polite. These are roughly the two major characteristics of the school. (May 23, Tokyo)

Local News

Request from the Business Reorganization Committee 105

To Restrict Gold Futures Trading

The Business Reorganization Committee sent letters yesterday to organizations such as the Gold Exchange, the Bankers Association, and the Foreign Banks Association regarding the restriction of gold futures trading. The letter stated: "We previously reported that the sharp rise in gold prices has greatly affected commerce and people's livelihoods. Various business organizations have repeatedly requested that appropriate measures be discussed and submitted to the authorities for remedy. The committee, mindful of the importance of its duties and aware of the complexity of the issue, has repeatedly held serious discussions with the financial sector and various organizations. It has consulted with representatives of the Bankers Association and the Money Exchange Association and agreed on four measures, which have been submitted to the Ministries of Finance and Industry for adoption and implementation. At the same time, letters have been sent to the relevant Chinese and foreign commercial firms for consideration. Currently, there are many opinions that the sharp rise in gold prices is due to speculation and manipulation, and there are proposals to suspend trading on the gold exchange as a remedy. This complex issue is not easy to resolve rashly. Moreover, futures trading actually has the effect of averaging commodity prices, so it would be wrong to ban it outright. However, the ratio of world prices to gold prices should be around two shillings, but it has now risen to around one shilling and five pence, which is clearly affected by large-scale speculative trading. Therefore, it seems that the opinions are not without merit. The committee believes that in order to prevent manipulation by speculators, any non-import/export businesses engaged in gold futures trading or foreign exchange that is not required for their business and is only aimed at gaining unexpected windfall profits should be restricted. This restriction will not hinder legitimate commercial activities and will reduce market turmoil. Therefore, Item 3 of the proposed remedial measures restricts non-import/export businesses from engaging in gold futures trading or purchasing foreign exchange. Banks' foreign exchange transactions are also limited to transactions with import/export businesses. After the implementation of this measure, the business of some of the relevant commercial firms may be reduced, but it can consolidate the overall situation of the Chinese and foreign commercial markets. When weighing the pros and cons, we hope to receive your support. We are sending this letter specifically to inform you and request that you take note and circulate it to your colleagues for handling."

No Excuses to Disrupt Rice Prices 108

The Social Affairs Bureau Reiterated the Prohibition

Recently, a small number of rice shops and rice merchants in this city have colluded to disrupt public order and secretly purchased white rice at discounted prices. Yesterday, the Social Affairs Bureau issued an order to the Rice Trade Organization's Reorganization Committee, stating: "We have received a report from the committee stating that rice prices in the northern market have become chaotic again. Merchants are demanding prices that exceed the limited prices and refuse to sell at lower prices. The market is being controlled by the merchants. If this situation continues, the committee will be unable to maintain the limited prices. According to this, if there is evidence that merchants are disrupting the limited prices, they should be severely punished to maintain the rice market. The industry should name and report these merchants instead of using ambiguous language to evade responsibility. We hereby order the Reorganization Committee to inform the industry to strictly abide by the limited prices and not to disrupt the market. If any merchants are found to be refusing to sell or are secretly discounting prices, they should be reported to the bureau immediately for investigation. Any rice shops or merchants who fail to report and are secretly discounting prices will be punished together."

Mongolian Conference Delegation

Passed Through Shanghai Yesterday for Sightseeing in Hangzhou 110

Inner Mongolian Representatives Talk About the Conference

A delegation of more than 70 representatives to the Mongolian Conference arrived in Shanghai by train from Beijing at 4:30 PM yesterday. With the exception of a few representatives from Rehe who stayed in Shanghai, the rest took the 5:55 PM train to Hangzhou for sightseeing. The Zhejiang Provincial Government sent representatives to Shanghai to welcome them. Wu Heling and Anhui Provincial Chairman Yan Fuxiang did not come due to illness. Our reporter interviewed Tong Jizhong, a representative of the Zosutu League of Rehe, at the train station yesterday and asked about the conference. He replied that the decisions regarding Mongolian education were made in accordance with the resolutions of the Second National Education Conference. Regarding administrative organizations, the Mongolian representatives initially proposed that each league organize a League Government with a Banner Government under it. However, the terminology was deemed inappropriate, so it was changed to a League Public Office with one League Chief and one Deputy League Chief, one Assistant Officer, and one Military Officer. Each League is completely independent and directly under the Central Government. Under the League Public Office is the Banner Public Office, which is headed by one Banner Chief with powers similar to those of an administrative officer. Under him are a number of Banner Affairs Officers, the number of which depends on the size of the banner: six for large banners, four for medium banners, and two for small banners. As for military affairs, it was decided to organize a security team on a banner basis, with ten to twenty men from each company. Large banners have about twenty companies, so the number of security team members is about 200 to 400. The weapons and equipment will be subsidized by the Central Government. In general, this conference was not entirely satisfactory, but everything cannot be accomplished overnight. Therefore, we hope for gradual improvement. Our delegation plans to take a boat to Tianjin in a few days and then return to Suiyuan by land. One more thing that is noteworthy from the conference is that the Zhangjia Living Buddha's office in Beijing submitted a document to the Executive Yuan denying the Inner Mongolian representatives and the resolutions. The representatives issued a declaration opposing this. Since the Zhangjia Living Buddha is the head of Lamaism, he has no right to interfere in administrative matters. Therefore, the conference has decided to abolish the Lama Temple Printing Office organization to prevent administrative chaos.

New US Tariff Rates to Be Implemented 115

Greatest Impact on Chinese Goods

According to sources from the US Commercial Office in Shanghai, the new tariff rates, which were last revised by the US government, will be announced and implemented this week. The revisions include tariff increases on 887 imported goods, tariff reductions on 233 goods, and the imposition of tariffs on 48 goods that were previously duty-free. The tariffs on most Chinese goods exported to the United States have been increased significantly. Therefore, the implementation of the new tariff rates will have the greatest impact on Chinese exporters. The details of the tariff rates will be known after they are announced.

Anqing Public Wharf Case

Open Letter from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to the People of Anhui 116

Opposing Economic Invasion by Foreign Merchants

Upholding the Development of National Shipping Rights

Regarding the matter of setting up a public wharf in Anqing, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company believes that the Anhui Provincial Government's reply has not fundamentally revoked or prohibited foreign ships from docking. The company considers this matter to be of great importance and yesterday issued a declaration urging the people of Anhui to support the development of Chinese shipping rights. The declaration stated: Our company has always attached importance to river transport and wharf facilities. We have both superior and newer, faster ships. Recently, the nation has taken over the foundation of the domestic shipping industry, and we observe the ardent expectations of the people. We strive to strengthen ourselves and dare not slacken, hoping to recover shipping rights and reduce losses. However, the economic invasion by foreign merchants is not a matter of a single day. We must rely on everyone's collective efforts to achieve success. The Yangtze River shipping rights are gradually declining, and the Chinese people are working hard to recover them. Fortunately, the port of Anqing remains intact, and foreign ships cannot dock according to the treaty. This is a rare achievement. How should the Chinese people cherish it? Our company deeply feels the importance of its responsibilities and has never imitated foreign ships in hoarding and monopolizing. We are working hard to rectify ourselves to benefit the people of Anhui (omitted middle section). The water freight prices have increased significantly in various ports, but Anqing is the only port with lower freight for the largest volume of exports, and passenger ticket prices remain at the old rates of ten years ago. Our company's special-class ships are significantly cheaper than ordinary foreign ships by 20%. We do everything in our power to reduce the burden on the Chinese people. Our company has moved the newly renovated Wuhu wharf, which cost tens of thousands of dollars, to Anqing for use. Passengers going up and down the river are not charged any fees. We have eight ships running on the Yangtze River, which are sufficient for cargo and passenger needs. If there is a cargo backlog, we can add more seagoing ships at any time. All these facts are known to the world. If there are any shortcomings, they are inevitable. We express our sincere intentions to seek guidance from our fellow countrymen. The prosperity or decline of our company's affairs is related to the nation's shipping rights and the honor and disgrace of the people of Anhui.

The Chinese Cigarette Industry

Yesterday's Petition to Party and Government Organs 117

Stating the Painful Situation

Requesting Relief

The Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Manufacturers Association has recently decided to send representatives to Beijing to petition for relief due to the deteriorating environment and the imminent collapse of their businesses. It was also decided that before this, each factory, together with representatives of their workers, would make a preliminary request for relief from the city's party, government, and tax authorities to strengthen their efforts. This was previously reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the city's petition event took place yesterday. At 8:00 AM, no less than two hundred male and female workers from various cigarette factories gathered before and behind the association's premises. More than ten cars were prepared. Around 9:00 AM, they proceeded one after another to the City Party Headquarters at Baiyun Temple. Each person held a white flag with various slogans written on them, such as "Implement the Principle of People's Livelihood to relieve factory and worker life," "Break economic aggression," "Implement equal treatment, abolish narrow tax revenues," and "Demand a box flower system and promote domestic goods." They chanted slogans, and the order was excellent. At the gate of the Party Headquarters, they got out of the cars together and lined up. The petition representatives, Lao Jingxiu, Yao Jixian, Bao Gengsheng, etc., went to see the City Executive Committee, where they were received by Committee Member Tao Baichuan, who inquired in detail about the various painful situations of the Chinese factories. He agreed to discuss the matter properly and forward it to the Central Party Headquarters for consideration and relief. He also agreed to request the tax rules files from the Cigarette Unified Tax Office for research. The representatives were very satisfied and expressed their gratitude before leaving. They then went to the City Government at Fenglin Bridge to petition. They were received by Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, where the chief representative, Lao Jingxiu, etc., reiterated the painful situation and requested relief. They were promised that methods of relief would be discussed and urgently submitted to the National Government for approval. They then went to the Social Affairs Bureau at Xiaonanmen, where they expressed their pain as before. It was already lunchtime, and the office was closed. Chen Zeyi accepted the petition and promised to convey it to the director and urgently seek relief. They then led the team to the Chamber of Commerce and had a brief rest in the assembly hall. The representatives stated the reasons for the petition, and committee members Wang Yansong, Wang Xiaolai, and Yu Zhihao received them and discussed the matter for a long time. They promised to do their best to help. Then, the team went to the Cigarette Unified Tax Office of the Ministry of Finance on Sanma Road at the Customs House, where Secretary Dong Zhongding received them. In addition to promising to forward the request to the Ministry of Finance to relieve the pain of the Chinese factories, he also resolved two local issues: (1) It is proposed that Hebei flower stamps be exempted from export tax by analogy with the sales in the Jin-Sui area. (2) All officials and subordinates are notified that they must protect cigarette merchants in tax administration and must not be overly punitive. During these six hours, the hundreds of people acted appropriately and did not cause any accidents. The energy spent by the leaders of the various teams and the leading representatives was truly remarkable. The petition submitted to the City Party Headquarters and the City Government is recorded below (omitting titles): The Chinese cigarette industry relies heavily on American tobacco as raw material to cater to the needs of society. Three years ago, the exchange rate of US dollars to Shanghai taels was about 70 taels per 100 US dollars. Recently, it has plummeted to between 34 and 35 taels. The surge in gold prices has broken all previous records. The cost has increased more than doubled compared to before. If we want to increase prices, we are restricted by tax levels, and the price increase is not enough to offset the cigarette tax of the sixth grade. If we want to close down, it will hinder the livelihoods of workers. Worker unemployment is related to social stability. Therefore, the situation of Chinese cigarette merchants today is that they cannot make a living by advancing, and they cannot close down by retreating. They have reached a dead end. On the 6th of this month, the association convened an emergency meeting and resolved three relief measures, which were telegraphed to the Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Finance and Industry for review. So far, we have not received any approval. Assuming the government agrees to provide relief, there is still hope of coming back to life. Otherwise, it can be said with certainty that the dozens of remaining cigarette factories and tens of thousands of cigarette factory workers will all become successors to Nanyang within a year. Now, representatives have been jointly elected by various factories to petition together. We humbly request that our Ministry (City) Chiefs provide unified assistance, forward the same-day telegram and request to the Yuan and Ministry for approval of the three relief measures, and sincerely accept it, so that our Chinese cigarette industry can continue to survive for a while and leave a glimmer of hope. The pain of being captured is a matter of life and death, and we do not choose our words urgently. We sincerely hope that you will understand.

People's Defence Corps

Formulating Service Regulations for Corps Members 127

The Organizing Committee of the Shanghai People's Defense Corps has formulated service regulations for corps members and submitted them to the Municipal Government for record in order to rectify discipline and provide a standard for corps members' services. It has been approved and is now recorded as follows: Article 1: All members of the People's Defense Corps of this city (hereinafter referred to as "members"), whether paid or unpaid, shall abide by the provisions of these regulations. Article 2: Members shall understand the Party's meaning and abide by the Party's program, and their sole duty shall be to protect local tranquility. They shall not have any behavior that exceeds the rules. Article 3: Without the orders and leadership of their superiors, members shall not enter people's homes, arrest people, or search for objects under the pretext of arresting bandits. Article 4: If a member detects the whereabouts of bandits, he shall immediately report to his superior for verification and handling. He shall not arrest them without authorization. Article 5: A member who captures a bandit shall immediately send him and the stolen goods to his direct superior for disposal according to law. He shall not dispose of them without authorization. Article 6: Members shall arrive on time for tasks and assignments and shall not be late. Article 7: Members shall not be absent from or late for training without reason. Article 8: If a member has an accident or illness, he shall apply for leave to his direct superior in advance. It shall be valid after approval. The same applies to those requesting long leave (leave application rules will be formulated separately). Article 9: Members are not allowed to wear uniforms during non-service and training hours. They must dress neatly and wear armbands. Article 10: When a member in uniform encounters someone who should be saluted, he shall give the appropriate salute. The etiquette is the same as that of the army. Article 11: Unless otherwise specified, members' firearms and bullets shall be kept by themselves. They shall be cleaned and carefully preserved on weekdays. If there is any damage, it shall be repaired immediately so that they can be used at any time. Article 12: Firearms and bullets shall not be carried casually or fired without reason during non-service and training hours. Article 13: Members' firearms and bullets shall be reported by the group to which they belong to the Organizing Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Organizing Committee") for numbering, branding, registration, and filing. Article 14: If each group needs to add arms to its strength, it shall first report to the superior for approval from the Organizing Committee before purchasing, and handle it in accordance with the provisions of Article 13. Article 15: Members shall do their best to be amiable and caring for the local people and shall not be lazy, arrogant, or abuse their power. Article 16: Matters of rewards and punishments for members shall be temporarily handled in accordance with the provisions of Articles 22 to 26 of the County People's Defense Corps Law promulgated by the central government before separate provisions are made in this city. Article 17: If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be revised at any time. Article 18: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation by the Organizing Committee and shall be reported to the Municipal Government for record.

Tragic Situation of the Bandit Disaster in Boxian County 129

Report from the Jisheng Association

The China Jisheng Association has recently received a telegram from Guo Wenche, Zhang Yingtao, Li Xiangding, and Li Xianyi, representatives of the disaster victims in Hao County, stating that in the winter of the Republic of China year 14, tens of thousands of bandits attacked Hao County and occupied it for more than twenty days, burning, killing, looting, and seizing without any humanity. Your association generously donated huge sums of money, and Mr. Liu Lingsheng, Mr. Wang Yixian, and others personally went to the disaster area to distribute relief and save countless lives. Last year, Huang Hui in Hao South incited chaos and looted houses, turning them into ruins. The people were half buried in ditches. This spring, the bandits returned to Hao and stationed tens of thousands of people, imposing exorbitant taxes and levies, leaving ten houses empty out of ten. Livestock was used for military purposes, farmers stopped farming, and the livelihood was cut off. As the war started, Hao City was besieged, firewood and food were exhausted, and bombs were flying, causing more horrific deaths and injuries than in the past. Now, the bandits in Hao County are besieged in the city, and the hungry soldiers are seizing food from the people. The people cannot escape and can only sit and wait for death. The tragedy of exchanging children and dissecting corpses is happening again. We beg you to generously donate huge sums of money to save lives, and we will not be able to await your orders. Since there is no clean land in Anhui Province, in addition to the association's previous relief efforts in Wu, Xuan, Chu and other counties, the association is now short of manpower and financial resources and is at a loss.

Sanbei Compatriots

Initiate Dredging of Fenghu Lake in Fengpu, Sanbei 130

Fenghu Lake in Longshan, Fengpu, Sanbei covers an area of more than 1,000 acres and is needed for irrigation in various villages in Dongxu Township. Due to years of disrepair, reeds and reeds have grown. Last month, when the mourning ceremony for Mrs. Yu Qiaqing was held, the fellow villagers gathered together. Yu Qiaqing, Yu Hexi, Dong Xunquan, Zheng Xitang and others proposed to repair the lake, estimating the dredging cost at 150,000 yuan. The initiators have committed 50,000 yuan.
