Yu Qiaqing presided over the meeting and continued to raise funds. Zhu Zubing committed 5,000 yuan, and Lin Xiuliang committed 3,000 yuan. The Zhenhai Highway Bureau has been entrusted to send personnel to measure and sample, and construction is scheduled to start in October and be completed in two years. In the future, not only will the scenery of Longshan be the crown of the townships in the three counties, but also the farmers will benefit greatly.

British American Tobacco Factory

Resolution of the Strike Wave of Female Workers 132

The British American Tobacco Company's new and old factories in Pudong, female workers in the tobacco leaf workshop caused a strike wave due to disagreement with the factory's change of work. Labor and management held on for many days without resolving the situation. Various situations have been reported in previous newspapers. It is now learned that yesterday morning, City Party Department representative Wu Jiaze and Social Affairs Bureau representative Qiu Peihua, together with union representatives Chen Peide, Gu Ruofeng, and Ye Huibing, continued to visit the factory for the second step of mediation. After long negotiations, the factory recognized the workers' demands: (1) In the future, the work will be calculated at five jiao and five fen per person per day. The standard is 325 pounds of tobacco leaves. If less, wages will be deducted at a standard of one jiao and six fen. If more, it will be added accordingly. (2) Wages during the strike period will be paid at four jiao and five fen per person per day from the 2nd. Each female worker felt satisfied, and it was declared a satisfactory solution. Therefore, work has resumed at 1:00 PM. It is also learned that the working hours of the British American Tobacco Factory workers have been ten hours. The union has now submitted a request to the National Government to instruct the factory to change it to nine hours to regulate the spirit of the workers. The factory has also unanimously followed this from yesterday.

Local News Two

Pronouncement of Verdict in the Case of Serial Matricide 134

Four Convicts, Zhang Wenqing and Others, Sentenced to Death

The Funds for Zhang Su's Coffin and Burial Are All Outstanding

Official Order to Recover and Manage the Confiscated Money

Zhang Wenqing, a woman from Huzhou residing at No. 762 Bian'de Road, colluded with Chen Hengcai, Yao Yonggui, and Gao Jintang to murder her stepmother, Zhang Su, aged 34, with a knife in her residence at approximately 6 p.m. on January 25th of this year, due to a dispute over inheritance. The case was investigated by Chinese Detective Lang Jintang and Western Detective Chief MacWhirter of the Jing'an Temple Police Station, who apprehended the four male and female suspects and handed them over to the court. After more than ten interrogations, the debate concluded last Tuesday, and the date for the verdict announcement was set. As reported in this newspaper yesterday, at 2:30 p.m. the police escorted the male and female convicts to the Third Criminal Division of the Special Court. Police lawyers Ru Baoyi and Wang Yaotang, as well as defense lawyers for the accused, were present in court awaiting instructions. At 2:30 p.m., Judge Wu Tingqi, the original trial judge, took the bench and began reading the main text: "Defendants Zhang Wenqing and Chen Hengcai, each found guilty of instigating murder, are each sentenced to death and deprived of civil rights indefinitely. Yao Yonggui and Gao Jintang, each found guilty of jointly conspiring to murder, are each sentenced to death and deprived of civil rights indefinitely. If dissatisfied, they may file an appeal within ten days. Witness Gong Chunfu's bail of 200 yuan is approved for return." The plaintiff's lawyer, Fan, stated that several hundred yuan had already been spent on funeral expenses for Zhang Su after her death, and all were outstanding. Therefore, he requested that the recovered banknotes and bank draft of 400 yuan be released first to settle the debts. There was also a bank draft for 2,000 taels, which could be transferred to the civil court for processing. Judge Wu then replied, "The case file contains Shanghai Day and Night Bank deposit slips for 400 yuan and banknotes totaling 45 yuan, which are approved to be handed over to Zhang Wenheng (i.e., the deceased's son) along with her uncle, Su Yaoting (i.e., Su Xiaoting), to obtain reliable shopkeepers as guarantors and temporarily collect the funds to cover the coffin and burial expenses of the late Zhang Su. A detailed list of the expenses should be submitted and attached to the file." After the verdict was announced, the four convicts were separately detained by the police pending execution after confirmation. This heinous case of familial betrayal is the first of its kind since Zhang Xin Sheng and is highly regarded by society. The police investigation was also very thorough, solving the case quickly without missing a single suspect. Prosecutor Ru Baoyi was particularly able to base his arguments on legal principles, repeatedly debating in each court hearing. Now that the perpetrators have been punished according to the law, the grievance of the deceased has been redressed. Therefore, the bereaved family is very grateful to the police for fulfilling their duties and upholding the law.

Huzhou Small Steamer

Robbery on the Yong'an Steamer 135

Old Helmsman Dies a Tragic Death

All Passengers Robbed Clean

The Xin Yong'an steamer, a Huzhou-bound steamer of the Yong'an Steamship Company's Shanghai branch, located at No. 150 Shanxi Road, South Bank of the Pot Soup Alley Bridge in this city, was en route from Huzhou to Shanghai at around 3 p.m. the day before yesterday. As it was sailing in the Suzhou Creek, passing the Lihui area east of Luxu, it was suddenly surrounded by over a hundred bandits on both banks and in the water on three sides. They fired shots and ordered the ship to stop. The old helmsman, Huang Genxiang, seeing the bandits swarming like ants and being very fierce, dared not confront them. He immediately rang the bell to stop the engine and await orders. However, the bandits were very impatient and fired shots like rain. Huang Genxiang was suddenly struck in the head by a bullet while on the side of the ship. He immediately fell to the ground and died due to his injuries. The bandits then swarmed onto the ship and wantonly robbed all the passengers, over a hundred in total, without exception. The losses were estimated at around 6,000 gold yuan.

The Xin Yong'an steamer departed from Huzhou at 7 a.m. the day before yesterday, traveling slowly and arriving in Shanghai. At around 3 p.m., after passing Luxu and traveling east for about three li, the place was named Lihui. The distance from Huzhou to here was about 160 li. The distance from Lihui to Shanghai was also the same. This was about halfway. The waterway was very narrow, and the banks were close enough to call out to each other. Villagers were engaged in fishing, and many large nets were placed in the water. Small steamers passing through this area had to slow down for fear of obstructing the fishing nets. At that time, the Yong'an steamer was proceeding slowly when suddenly gunshots were heard from the shore, first sparse and then dense. The old helmsman, Huang Genxiang, was on the side of the ship, directing the steering. Hearing the sound, he knew something was wrong and quickly ordered the helmsman to stop the engine. However, in the rush, although the engine stopped, the forward momentum did not cease, and the ship continued to move forward with the remaining momentum. Moreover, the rattling sound of the engine came from the middle cabin, as if the ship was steaming forward. The bandits misunderstood and fired even more urgently, aiming their guns at the wheelhouse. A bullet flew and struck the old helmsman Huang Genxiang in the temple. He immediately fell to the ground with a thud, blood flowing from his forehead. He fainted and did not move, and the ship came to an abrupt stop.

The bandits, numbering over a hundred, swarmed onto the ship from small boats. They were armed with fierce weapons and quick-firing guns, and their voices sounded as if they came from Shandong province. The bandits wore various clothing, including blue cloth shirts and pants, and tattered military uniforms. Those who appeared to be leaders directed the crowd to rob in separate directions. Passengers on the Huzhou steamer were mostly wealthy merchants from various classes along the Suzhou Creek. The bandits targeted everyone, from first class to the canopy, and no one escaped. Everything, including money, clothes, jewelry, and luggage, was robbed by the bandits. Even the fruits carried by the passengers, such as peaches, were taken. If passengers were wearing silk shirts and pants, the bandits would exchange them for short blue cloth jackets and pants. The ship was robbed clean from bow to stern, and the commotion lasted for about an hour before the bandits carried away their loot and fled with a shout. The old helmsman, Huang Genxiang, was already barely breathing. He closed his eyes and died shortly after the bandits left the ship. He was sixty-three years old and an old helmsman.

The Yong'an steamer usually arrived in Shanghai at around 8 p.m. That night, it arrived about an hour and a half late. The company officials were worried and anxious. When the steamer docked, they learned the whole story of the ordeal. The passengers disembarked, all in a state of disarray, with incomplete clothing and without hats and shoes. Some even disembarked barefoot because the bandits had taken their satin shoes and leather boots. They searched everything, even the grass hats and felt hats. The purser on the ship temporarily claimed to be a tea servant to avoid disaster. After arriving in Shanghai, the passengers discussed how to deal with the aftermath. They did not return to their hometowns until yesterday, instead staying temporarily with relatives and friends in Shanghai. The damage to the ship itself was small, but there were three or four bullet holes in the wheelhouse, which was terrifying to see. According to those who traveled on the ship, the Yong'an steamer had been targeted by bandits three days earlier when it departed from Shanghai to Luxu, but fortunately, it steamed away and was not detained. Perhaps the bandits knew that Huzhou was a wealthy area and that merchants traveling to Shanghai would carry a lot of money, so robbing them would be profitable. However, it is tragic that an old helmsman in his sixties died a violent death.

Zhu Jixing Arrested

Yesterday's Court Interrogation 136

Zhu Admits to Embezzling Huge Sums

Due to Losses in the Sugar Trade

Intended to Repay After Fleeing

But Credit Was Lost

Zhu Jixing from Zhenhai was a deputy comprador at the British-owned Jardine Matheson Bank and also opened the Yuan Xingde Sugar Firm, incurring significant losses in the sterling exchange business. He engaged in various fraudulent activities, embezzling over 160,000 yuan from the bank. Unable to cover the losses, he absconded without a trace. The bank reported the matter to the police station, which issued a warrant for his arrest and offered a reward of 2,000 yuan. Since Zhu's escape, two Ningbo natives, Xie Tonghou and Yu Xilin, who were accountants at Jardine Matheson Bank, were suspected by the bank's Western staff of colluding in the fraud. The bank filed a lawsuit against them, and Chief Judge Xu Jiashi of the Special District Court opened the trial several times, ordering Xie and Yu to each post a bail of 30,000 yuan. The case was rescheduled for further hearing on the morning of the 21st of this month.

Circumstances of Zhu Jixing's Arrest At 2:40 p.m. on the afternoon of the day, Chinese detective Zhang Guisheng of the Avenue Foch Police Station received a tip that Zhu was hiding in the attic room of No. 1281 Xiang'an Lane, Seward Road. Detective Zhang, together with a Western detective, took the arrest warrant and proceeded to arrest him. Zhu was lying in bed when the detectives arrived. After examining him and confirming that his appearance matched the description on the arrest warrant, they arrested him and took him back to the police station. Because the case was being investigated by the General Police Station, he was transferred to that station for detention.

The police charged him with two crimes. Yesterday morning at 9 a.m., Chinese detective Fei Kelun escorted Zhu to the First Criminal Division of the Special Court, where Chief Judge Xu Jiashi and Chief Prosecutor Zhou Xianjue took the bench for interrogation. Gan Jingxian, the lawyer representing the police, stated that the police were prosecuting him under Articles 357 (embezzlement) and 224 (forgery) of the Criminal Law.

The Method of Altering Numbers Zhu altered the numbers on deposit slips made by others. His method was to change a deposit of 20,000 silver dollars made by Bao Feng Qian Zhuang into 2,000 on the receipt, get it signed by the Western staff, and then add a "0" after the "2000" in the English text, making it 20,000 again, and give it to the Qian Zhuang's partner. In this way, he embezzled 18,000 yuan. Similarly, 30,000 yuan was changed to 3,000 yuan. In total, there were eight deposit slips with altered numbers. However, before fleeing, when the Qian Zhuang came to redeem the deposits, Zhu managed to pay them back in full. The bank had to pay what was not repaid, incurring significant losses. Today, a representative from Jardine Matheson Bank is also present to testify.

Statement of Jardine Matheson's Representative Zhu Jixing's lawyer, Jiang Baoli, stated that he and lawyer Jiang Yiping jointly represented the defendant. According to the police, this case should be combined with the case of Xie Tonghou, so today's hearing must be postponed because they have not yet met with the client. Judge Xu stated that he needed to ask about the forgery of documents and summoned Hesituo, the representative of Jardine Matheson Bank, to the stand. Hesituo's statement about the alteration of tickets was largely the same as that of lawyer Gan, and he stated that the defendant had forged a total of 39 bank drafts, totaling 161,713 taels and 7 qian and 9 fen, and submitted the bank drafts as evidence.

Record of Zhu Jixing's Testimony Judge Xu reviewed the bank drafts and read out each date and amount, one by one. Zhu nodded repeatedly, saying that there were no errors. He also confessed that he had been with Jardine Matheson for fifteen years, starting as a deputy runner, then promoted to full runner, and then to his current position. His embezzlement of large sums was due to losses in the sugar trade and the large sums he had to pay as a guarantor. Last year, he used empty money for up to 256,000 yuan. On May 20th of this year, he paid the bank 37,000 taels of silver and 10,000 yuan in foreign currency. On the 21st, he paid another 4,000 taels of silver and 4,000 yuan in foreign currency. After his escape, he intended to repay within ten days, but the matter was published in various newspapers, causing his credit to be completely lost and making it impossible to raise funds. The alteration of the receipts was done using a type of medicine sold by the Commercial Press.

Chief Comprador Testifies Ling Pengji, the chief comprador of Jardine Matheson Bank, testified that he saw Zhu Jixing hand over 10,000 yuan to the bank at the time, but did not know the details of the rest. After reviewing the testimony, Judge Xu adjourned the case to be combined with the Xie case, and Zhu Jixing was remanded in custody.

The Forged Bank Draft Case Continuing the hearing on the case related to Zhu, Zheng Hekang, a partner in Zhu Jixing's Deji Sugar Firm, was accused of using forged bank drafts. On the 21st of last month, Zhu Jixing and his brother, Jiming, instructed Zheng to deposit a bank draft from Yifeng Qian Zhuang for 52,116 taels, 7 qian, and 6 fen into the Siming Bank. However, the bank discovered that the draft was forged and reported it to the General Police Station, which ordered detective Zhou Xiaozhi to detain Zheng and hand him over to the Special District Court. Zheng hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him, arguing that the defendant was acting on the orders of his employer and did not know that the draft was forged. The court adjourned the hearing and ordered Zheng to post a bail of 300 yuan. The details of this case were reported in this newspaper.

Zheng Hekang Granted Release Yesterday morning, Judge Xu questioned Zheng, who testified that Zhu Jixing gave him the draft. Judge Xu then ordered Zhu Jixing to stand in the witness box. Zhu readily admitted it. Lawyer Fan Gang immediately stated that Zhu Jixing's confession proved that the defendant Zheng Hekang was unaware of the forgery, and requested his release. The police lawyer Gan Jingxian also stated that since the defendant was unaware of the forgery, he should be released and the police should file a separate charge against Zhu Jixing. Judge Xu then declared him not guilty and cancelled his bail.

Haunted by His Former Wife

Sliced Open in a Dream 137

Wife's Solicitude for Her Children at the Time of Death

Insistent Instructions Never to Remarry

Breach of Promise by Remarrying Only Six Mornings

Causing Painful Abdominal Rupture

Zhang Guisheng, a 43-year-old man from Jiangbei, worked as a laborer at the Samsung Yarn Factory in Yangshupu and rented a room near Workshop No. 88. At around 5 a.m. yesterday morning, he used a razor to cut open his abdomen, removing his internal organs and causing blood to flow into a stream. Initially, his wife suspected that he was wetting the bed, but then she smelled blood and knew something was wrong. She rushed forward and saw Zhang's abdomen covered in blood, a horrific sight. She was shocked and immediately ordered her daughter to report to the police station. The Chinese police from No. 226 arrived and transported him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Afterwards, according to Zhang, his first wife had passed away six years ago and had given birth to a son and a daughter. The eldest daughter, named Gendi, is now fifteen years old, and the son, named Liusesizi, is eleven years old. When his deceased wife was seriously ill, she had said to Zhang, "If I die, you don't need to remarry. I have already given you children. If you remarry, my children will undoubtedly suffer abuse from your stepmother. If you break this promise, I will make you uneasy in the afterlife." At that time, he had promised her wholeheartedly, and his wife had passed away with a smile. For six years, all was well. Last month, through the kindness of a friend, he introduced Zheng, a young woman from his hometown, to be his wife. She was 32 years old. Only six mornings after she entered the door, this tragic incident occurred. In reality, it was caused by his former wife in a dream. He did not feel any pain when he cut open his abdomen.

Public Bus Ticket Seller

Honest Find 138

Japanese Person Leaves Behind Banknotes

Amounting to Approximately Two Thousand Yuan

At approximately 4 p.m. the day before yesterday, a Japanese person from a certain yarn factory was carrying a package of banknotes, approximately 2,000 yuan in foreign currency, intended for paying wages. Due to a hurried exit from the public bus on the Jing'an Temple to Bazichang route of the Public Bus Company of the Public Concession, he left the banknotes in the vehicle. A certain ticket seller noticed the large sum of cash and immediately reported it to the ticket inspector. The ticket inspector sent the banknotes to the company. Before long, the Japanese person went to the company to report the loss, and after verifying that the amount matched, he completed the procedures and retrieved it. Subsequently, the Japanese person gave the ticket inspector and the ticket seller several yuan in foreign currency as a reward. Such a ticket seller can be said to be honest.

Feng Bingnan

Welcoming and Farewell Party for the Editor of the North-China Daily News 139

Farewell Banquet for Mr. Grien Departing for His Home Country

Welcome Reception for Mr. Harvard Arriving in China

Page 16

Mr. Grien, editor of the North-China Daily News, will return to England on the 21st of this month. Feng Bingnan gathered prominent figures from the business and media sectors at his private residence last night at 7 p.m. to hold a farewell banquet for him, while also welcoming Mr. Harvard, the successor to the newspaper's editorship, to attend. Among those present were Yu Qiaqing, Rong Desheng, Lu Bohong, Qin Runqing, Zhang Zhuping, Wang Yingbin, Xiong Shaohao, Li Haoran, Wang Zhongwei, Yan Duhe, as well as Western merchants, totaling more than thirty people. During the event, Mr. Feng rose to deliver a farewell speech, stating that Mr. Grien had been in charge of the North-China Daily News for more than ten years. Although his views and opinions on various Chinese issues may not have been entirely agreed upon, his intentions were quite sincere. In the past, there were many misunderstandings between China and the West. In recent years, they have gradually approached each other and there is a growing understanding. The world advocates mutual assistance between China and foreign countries, which is easy to talk about but difficult to implement. To achieve true mutual assistance, it is necessary to seek mutual understanding. To seek understanding, it is necessary to meet and exchange opinions with each other from time to time. Tonight, we have specially invited Chinese and Western media to gather together. On the one hand, we bid farewell to Mr. Grien, hoping that he will share his experiences in China over the past ten years with his countrymen, which will not only benefit his countrymen but also promote the glory of China. On the other hand, we welcome Mr. Harvard to succeed Mr. Grien as editor of the newspaper. He will surely promote the goodwill between Chinese and foreign people with a spirit of mutual assistance. Mr. Harvard has been running newspapers in India for more than twenty years. Two years ago, he was summoned back to England to serve in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. This year, he is in charge of the North-China Daily News in China. He will surely use the skills of a statesman to benefit the friendship between China and foreign countries. Mr. Feng also composed a poem to present to Mr. Grien: "Who can carry the large pen? A literary giant holds a strong talent. The work is troublesome and difficult, but he can master it. The dangerous and suspicious shocks the demons. The opinions of the people are numerous and immeasurable. His electric eyes brightly illuminate the walls. He uses a model to first enclose the world. All things follow the round and square. Weighing wisdom is unparalleled. He can expand his duties and expand his words loudly. He can also evaluate people's shortcomings, whether beautiful or derogatory, it should be. Your opinion and my opinion may differ. What does it matter? The purpose is magnificent to each other. You are always busy for the public, seeking their welfare and auspiciousness. We lived together in Shanghai like duckweed, exhausting our efforts to protect and shield, ensuring that the fragile and precarious reaches Kangzhuang. Sometimes the path is dark and confused, and there are no lights to guide or mislead. But I believe you will never forget to be single-minded and not blind. Why do I trust you firmly? Because I wrote an article for you at that time. You can have confidence and sincerity. I hope you can still help my country. I hope you can still express your heart. You board the ship high and float across the ocean. The good feelings of friends are carried along. Just like the setting sun, the infinite good scenery is beyond the morning light. Your writing is fast and sincere. You can seek peace and prosperity for our country. You can seek welfare for our country. The benefits are great, and I will always hope for it."

Mr. Grien's reply mainly stated that the weekly publication of the North-China Daily News has been established for eighty years, and the North-China Daily News has a history of sixty years. He has only been in charge of the editorship for nineteen and a half years. Speaking of the long history of the North-China Daily News, nineteen years is just a blink of an eye. As Mr. Feng said, not everyone necessarily agrees with my opinions and propositions, and everyone has faults, how can I not? But I deeply believe that what I have written has all been sincere. A Western proverb says that sincerity is most likely to lead people to hell. As for this saying, I believe that my opinion will not lead people to prison and I deeply believe that it will not lead its readers to hell. He also said that he also had a penchant for poetry when he was young, but no one gave him poetry throughout his life. Now that he has received Mr. Feng's poem, he will cherish it as a treasure. The banquet lasted until after eleven o'clock, and the guests and hosts parted happily.

Municipal Electric Inspection Committee

Continued Inspection of Films 143

Film Advertisements Must Indicate "Inspected"

Since the establishment of the Shanghai Municipal Film Inspection Committee, it has been closely reviewing films in this city. Film merchants have also learned from the experience of the Great Light Cinema, so any new film must be submitted to the committee for inspection in advance to avoid disputes. Last week, there was news of a temporary suspension of inspections, and theaters in the concessions inquired about the matter with the committee. After the committee published a correction in the newspaper, they finally understood the truth. However, most of the film advertisements in Shen Xin two newspapers in recent days have not indicated "Inspected." The committee also made no indication. Yesterday, a reporter from Guomin News visited Chen Duanzhi, a member of the committee. According to him, the failure of the theaters' advertisements to indicate "Inspected" in recent days may be due to a misprint in a certain newspaper last week about a temporary suspension of inspections. However, the work of the committee has not stopped. It is now separately notifying the theaters to correct the error immediately. If there is any intentional delay, it should still be dealt with according to the regulations. It is also learned that the committee plans to compile and publish the details of the past year's work and the inspection catalog at the end of the year.

During a Raid on Bandits, a Detective's Pocket is Picked, Leading to a Shooting 144

In the New Shanghai Hotel

Eight Robbers Apprehended One After Another

At 2:30 p.m. yesterday, the Huishi Police Station of the Public Concession received a confidential report that a large number of bandits who had committed major crimes were hiding in Room 33 of the New Shanghai Hotel, No. 249 Jiu'an Lane, Wuma Road. After receiving the report, the police chief immediately ordered six Chinese and Western detectives to secretly proceed to the hideout with weapons. When the detectives entered the room, they saw four or five people inside talking and laughing enthusiastically. Upon seeing the detectives arrive, they panicked. One of the detectives told them to raise their hands. However, one person was slow to raise his hands and tried to reach into his pocket as if to retrieve something. To preemptively strike, the detectives fired two shots, hitting the robber in the right waist, causing him to fall to the ground. The other robbers were also apprehended and taken to the police station. The injured robber was sent to the Municipal Council Hospital by a Western police vehicle for treatment. To eliminate the bandits, the police chief dispatched several detectives to guard the hotel for several hours, and three or four more people were apprehended one after another, totaling eight people. Among them was a female bandit named Zhou, who was about twenty years old. She was transferred to the Special District Court for investigation this morning. According to reports, on the 11th, a local person named Xia Jinsheng, 32 years old, brought Zhou to open Room 33. After that, several people came and went every day, but they all looked like hooligans.

Apprehended Six Robbers in Zhabei 145

A Carpenter Falls to His Death in the River 148

A carpenter named Zhuang Xingfu, 23 years old and from Ningbo, married a woman named Wang Zhaodi, also 23 and from the same hometown. At that moment, the Jiangtian steamship passed by, its waves violently churning the water, sweeping Zhuang away without a trace. Zhang Xiaogouzi's Examination Confirms Drowning 150

The Blue Funnel Wharf recently received the Kai Xiang ship, which was loaded with coal. The foreman ordered the laborers to unload it. Woman Files for Divorce 152

Zhou Wanzhen, a woman from Changzhou who resides at number 80, south of Haichao Temple, Lujiabang, Shanghai, is a beautiful, fashionably dressed woman in her early twenties. In March of last year, through a matchmaker, she was betrothed to Shen Wenbin. A betrothal gift of one thousand yuan was received. Their wedding date was set for the 9th day of the 9th lunar month of this year. Shen, a native of this place, is 24 years old and studying medicine under the famous doctor Shen Zhuoru. Recently, Zhou hired a lawyer and filed a petition with the Special District Court, requesting permission to dissolve her marriage with Shen Wenbin. Her reason was that at the time of the engagement, she was in her hometown of Wujin and the decision was made entirely by her parents without her consent. When she returned to Shanghai and learned of the matter, she immediately stated her unwillingness. However, the Shen family deliberately advanced the wedding date, which was not her desire. The court accepted the petition and issued a summons for both parties. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Yi presided over the hearing in the Tenth Civil Court. The defendant, Shen Wenbin, was represented by lawyer Shen Qi. The plaintiff, Zhou Wanzhen, submitted her complaint, stating the aforementioned circumstances and requesting permission to dissolve the marriage. Then, the defendant's lawyer, Shen, stated that the case began with the plaintiff's lawyer sending a letter to his client requesting dissolution. The defendant then commissioned this lawyer to reply, agreeing to the dissolution but requiring the return of the one thousand yuan betrothal gift. The plaintiff's side stated that the betrothal gift was received by her parents and should be recovered from them. Later, last month, another letter was received from the plaintiff's lawyer agreeing to return the betrothal gift but requesting a slight delay. How could they send a letter on one hand and then file a lawsuit in the court on the other? This is truly strange. Now, the defendant's side, due to the plaintiff's actions, must file a counterclaim requesting confirmation of the validity of the marriage. Judge Yang, after reviewing the evidence and questioning the defendant Shen Wenbin, stated that both parties had an early intention to reconcile and there was no need for litigation. Since the plaintiff wished to dissolve the marriage, the betrothal gift should be returned. The plaintiff's lawyer then requested to withdraw the lawsuit, which the court granted.

Husband and Concubine Dissolve Relationship 153

Gu Yin Feng, a woman from Suzhou, is currently 21 years old. Previously, she was a prostitute in a brothel on East Xinqiao, French Concession. In July of the year before last, Xin Chunli, a tailor from Ningbo and the owner of Fachang Hongbang Tailor Shop at 931 and a half Broadway Road, frequented the brothel. He fell in love with Gu at first sight, and after much affection, they made a promise to be together forever. Xin paid to redeem Gu from prostitution and took her as his concubine. They lived together for two years. Recently, disagreements arose, and Gu hired lawyer E Sen to file a petition with the District Court, requesting to dissolve her relationship with Xin and demanding the return of her clothing and belongings. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Yi presided over the Tenth Civil Court. The plaintiff, Gu Yin Feng, stated that after marrying the defendant as a concubine, she lived with his first wife and suffered abuse. Therefore, in November of last year, she left. The defendant then invited many gangsters to come and cause trouble. She does not want to return and requests permission to leave and to recover her clothing and belongings. The defendant, Xin Chunli, stated that when the plaintiff was a prostitute, she was being abused by the evil madam, so he paid to redeem her and they lived together. Now that the plaintiff wants to leave, he is willing, but the clothing and belongings belong to him and cannot be returned. Judge Yang, with both parties willing to separate, suggested trying to reconcile and advised the defendant to return several items of the plaintiff's clothing. The defendant agreed, and a reconciliation was reached. The court clerk prepared a settlement document, which was signed by both parties and their lawyers, concluding the case.

The Responsibility of the Guarantor for Overdue Loans 156

Xiao Zhihe Sued for Loan

Xiao Chaoshi Implicated as Guarantor

Du Runsheng, represented by a lawyer, filed a lawsuit in the French Court, stating that in 1925, Xiao Zhihe borrowed 800 taels of silver from the plaintiff. At that time, Xiao Chaoshi, the owner of Yuanshun Pawnshop, guaranteed the loan. The loan agreement stated a term of six months. Afterwards, upon the expiration of the term, the debtor Xiao Zhihe was unable to repay the loan. The plaintiff has been giving him time to repay the loan until now, for six years, without receiving any payment. Moreover, the debtor has disappeared. The plaintiff requests permission to seek recovery from the guarantor. The defendant guarantor, Xiao Chaoshi, was also represented by a lawyer who argued that the loan agreement stated that the guarantor guaranteed the loan for a term of six months. Afterwards, the debtor repeatedly extended the term to the plaintiff, without notifying the guarantor. Now, six years have passed. According to civil law, since the term has expired, the guarantor is relieved of the responsibility of guaranteeing the loan. Furthermore, recently, the lawyer has also had a similar case representing a guarantor who was sued in the District Court and was dismissed by the court. He presented the judgment to the court for review. The plaintiff's lawyer argued for a long time. Judge Gong ordered that a date be set for the judgment to be announced.

Qianzhuang Creditors' Group

Opposes He Gengxing's Liquidation 157

After the collapse of Renhe and Hongyu Huiyu Hardware Stores on Catholic Church Street in the French Concession, the owner, He Gengxing, fled without a trace. Afterwards, it was found that the two stores owed more than one million yuan in debt. Banks and qianzhuang were owed more than 200,000 taels. Creditors such as Renheng, Henglai, Hengli, and Zhengda reported to the Qianye Gonghui, requesting that it forward a letter to the French Concession to oppose the appointment of a liquidator. The Shanghai Qianye Gonghui's letter to French Court Judge Gong yesterday is recorded below: Respectfully informing you that we recently received a joint letter from our fellow Qianzhuang, Renheng, Henglai, Yichang, Zhicheng, Henglong, Chengyu, Xinfu, Tongyu, Hengyu, Jiufeng, and Hengli and Zhengda Banks, stating that they had dealings with the Renhe and Hongyu Huiyu Hardware Stores on Catholic Church Street in the French Concession, amounting to more than 200,000 taels. The owner of the two stores, He Gengxing, recently absconded with the funds, and the two stores collapsed simultaneously. The direct losses suffered by the Qianzhuang are already so great, and the indirect impacts are even greater. Unexpectedly, after absconding with the funds, He Gengxing instigated others to falsely request the French Concession to order an accountant to carry out liquidation, which is obviously an illegal act to infringe upon the rights of the Qianzhuang creditors. As the Qianzhuang industry relates to Shanghai's finances, it should be protected according to law. The sudden collapse of Renhe and Hongyu Huiyu is a special circumstance and must be given special attention. We respectfully request that your court revoke the illegal liquidation procedures and strictly arrest He Gengxing, the owner of Renhe and Hongyu Huiyu, to investigate him and maintain financial security. The Qianzhuang Association has received this request and has determined that our fellow Qianzhuang, Renheng, and others have suffered greatly from the collapse of Renhe and Hongyu Huiyu. If their rights are harmed again, the impact will inevitably affect the overall financial situation. Therefore, we report this matter to you and request that your court immediately revoke the liquidation procedures for Renhe and Hongyu Huiyu and strictly arrest He Gengxing, the owner of the two stores, to investigate him and maintain financial security. This is a matter of public interest. Respectfully addressed to Judge Gong, French Concession. Shanghai Qianye Gonghui.

Datong Music Society Adds Summer Classes 165

The Datong Music Society on Songshan Road in the French Concession has initiated the study of the highest national music (Zhonghe Shaoyue). Last Sunday, the society formally practiced the music, and the results were excellent. The music has six movements: (1) Taihe Chapter, promoting the harmony of heaven and earth; (2) Xiehe Chapter, promoting the meaning of peace; (3) Tonghe Chapter, promoting the meaning of common peace; (4) Baohe Chapter, maintaining the meaning of peace; (5) Jihe Chapter, the meaning of permanent peace; (6) Xianghe Chapter, the meaning of being full of happiness. The musical instruments used are complete in all eight tones, and each team member can earnestly study. They will be able to give a public performance in about a month, making the highest national music of five thousand years come alive in the world. Isn't this a great event? It is also heard that because the summer vacation is approaching, many students from various schools are coming to the society to learn various national musical instruments, so the society has decided to open summer classes, divided into Qin, Se, Pipa, Silk Bamboo, and Beijing Opera systems. Using the simplest teaching methods, they will strive to ensure that each student gains something during the summer vacation (50 days). After the summer vacation, those with appropriate qualifications can join the society's large orchestra as formal members, and they can learn any musical instrument or piece of music for free, as a way to provide preferential treatment and cultivate more talent for national music.

Weather Report 166

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that the Yangtze River Basin would be mostly cloudy, while the southern region and Shandong area would be overcast. Recent News of Miss Yeh Hua, Detained by the Fujian Authorities 168

Originally, joy and sorrow, separation and reunion, occurred on the evening of January 6th. Lin Zhiyuan, Chen Naiyuan, Zheng Baojing, Cheng Shigui, Xu Xianshi, members of the Fujian Provincial Government, and Wu Shu, head of the Water Police Bureau, were detained by Lu's troops under the charge of being reactionary. The first three were sent to Yanping, and the latter three were escorted to Youxi. Great officials, who previously gathered day and night to discuss provincial affairs intimately, were thus forced to sing a farewell song. On April 6th, the six reunited, all confined in Hongshan Bridge, only eight miles away from the provincial capital. Soon, Commander Liu's troops arrived in Fuzhou, and the six were again imprisoned in Youxi. News of fortune and misfortune arrived frequently, and everyone was constantly surprised and delighted. It is said that comrades seek each other out, and those suffering from the same ailment sympathize with each other. However, comrades may sometimes not seek each other out, but those suffering from the same ailment always sympathize. These six individuals were both comrades and suffering from the same ailment; outsiders cannot know the feelings they experienced.

Lin and the others' meals and expenses are all the responsibility of Lu's troops. It is said they are treated well. The day after their detention, each was given one hundred yuan for visiting bamboo forests and smoking cigarettes. Meals cost three yuan per person per day, and although Fujian goods are expensive, this is enough for two meals of major dishes. However, it is not known how the Lin party felt when eating. According to those who know, Chen and Xu spend their days reading and practicing calligraphy, feeling quite at ease. They once said to others, "Gaining adversity in life can be beneficial for self-cultivation and career, so we are broad-minded." Hearing this is comforting, but thinking about it is very painful.

The news of life and death is certain. On the 9th of this month, various newspapers reported the news of Lin, Chen, and Cheng being killed. In fact, Lin Zhiyuan, Chen Naiyuan, and Xu Xianshi were beheaded in Yanping, while Cheng Shigui is still safe and sound. This was transmitted in a private telegram. Cheng's nephew, Ganhou, who returned from Fujian yesterday, also confirmed this. In a letter Cheng sent to a friend, a poem was attached, indicating that the author's report was not false. The poem is similar to the one by Luo Binwang of the Tang Dynasty when he was in prison. The poem says: "All day long I hear the sound of rain on the tower, spring comes and goes without sentiment.

Red Bean Anecdotes by Li Shuping

The red bean is originally a product of Lingnan. Unexpectedly, it also exists in Hunan. My friend, Mr. Yang Quansun, lives in Hengyang, and there are two red bean trees in his garden. Initially, he did not know about them. It was because a certain lady frequently visited the Yang family, and this lady was an advocate of homosexual love. Her lover suddenly went far away and sent a bean in a letter, calling it a "red bean rained down from heaven." The lady was extremely happy and showed it to Mr. Yang, considering it a rare treasure. Not long after, one day Yang was walking in his garden and found countless smooth red particles in the grass. He picked them up and saw that they were no different from the one the lady had shown him. He suspected that there might be a tree in the garden and searched everywhere, finally finding two trees. The branches and trunks were light green, like a parasol tree, and could be ten feet tall. The beans all grew like broad beans. As a result, people from far and near came to explore the curiosity, and for a time, the household was crowded. Recently, I received many pieces from Mr. Yang, red and beautiful. I still remember Chengzhai's notes, which said, "Red beans are bright red and never change for a thousand years." So I had them inlaid into rings and earrings as gifts for my wife, Di Hua, with unique beauty. Thus, I recorded the beginning and end of the story.

The Flower Festival has passed, and so has Qingming. Sending a lonely boat against the current, the dawn breeze blows through ten thousand mountains. In my dreams, I still talk of returning home." The title is "Song of Washing Stream Sand." His poem to his three friends says, "All laws should be abandoned, alas! People at crossroads, where to put this heart without joy or sorrow? Listen to the rain in the deep mountains, still singing of the spring of the earth. Diamond is originally indestructible, cherish this body in the water."

Mr. Cheng as I Know Him (Part 1) by Shen Zhuoran 169

Mr. Cheng's surname is Cheng, his given name is Ne, his style name is Dihua. He was originally from Anhui. He only lived in Shanghai since his grandfather's generation. In his youth, he focused on books and immersed himself in learning. Later, he studied the techniques of Shen Buhai and Han Fei, thus abandoning his original profession, but he did not achieve anything and soon gave it up and did something else. Later, he worked at the Progressive Bookstore and the New Shenbao Newspaper Office. When he was over fifty years old, the Datong Bookstore recruited him with courtesy to be the chief proofreader, and he ended his career there.

On the 8th of this month, which was a weekend, he returned home after a late-night drink and went to bed. His residence was a small three-room building with a cloth ladder outside the door. Mr. Cheng accidentally forgot about it and suddenly fell, seriously injured, and then died. Alas, how tragic! He usually did not reveal his age and only knew that he was just over sixty years old. Mr. Cheng's family was not wealthy, but rather poor. Since his father's time, Mr. Cheng did not know much about household finances. After his father died, he became the eldest brother, so he took care of family affairs a little, but he had lofty aspirations and did not engage in production. In a few years, the family became poorer, so he entrusted everything to his wife and stopped asking about it. It is said that his wife, Wu, was gentle and virtuous. Mr. Cheng initially admired the unrestrained style of Du Sijun, and often visited brothels and spent a lot of money. His wife heard about it slightly and tried to persuade him with subtle words. Mr. Cheng suddenly became angry and turned against her, but then regretted it. After his wife's death, he deeply blamed himself and from then on disappeared from the brothels.

He has two younger brothers. The second brother's right hand has been disabled since childhood, so he stays at home and lives off the family. The youngest brother is engaged in business, and the brothers are very affectionate and do not separate the property. He has four daughters, three of whom died young. The eldest daughter married a Tang from the same town. Her husband died early, leaving her a widow. Fortunately, she has a granddaughter, so she is determined to raise her orphan. Mr. Cheng used his income from writing to help her. When Mr. Cheng passed away, his daughter cried very sadly. The father-daughter relationship was indeed innate, and the suffering of the widow from now on will be unspeakable, which is especially sad.

Mr. Cheng was good at proofreading and had been engaged in this field for no less than twenty years. His writing style followed the Shuowen Jiezi. He regarded vulgar and broken characters as enemies and took pleasure in replacing them with true characters. If there were errors or questionable points in the manuscripts, he would definitely examine them carefully and then repair the gaps and correct the mistakes. He once said that modern education does not emphasize elementary studies, so even contemporary literary giants write carelessly and do not study them thoroughly, so shallow people are even less to blame. He was knowledgeable and had a strong memory. People with doubts would come to him for clarification, and Mr. Cheng would explain the origin without being impatient. Therefore, those who asked were all able to understand and were all happy to leave. When I first came to assist in proofreading, Mr. Cheng ignored me very much. Gradually, we became familiar, and he knew that I was not reckless and destructive, so he analyzed doubts and appreciated wonders with me, discussing the merits and demerits of ancient and modern literary figures. When our opinions differed, we argued with each other for days. When there was agreement, we admired each other.

A strange story overheard

Travel Notes from Nanyang (31) 170

26. I wanted to investigate the situation of squatters in this area. Their poverty is similar to the shacks outside Shanghai, or they live on a small boat. The top is steamed and the bottom is humid. They still put up door couplets, from which I know they are Chinese. The boatmen mostly travel in extremely dirty small rivers. The rickshaw pullers are mostly from Fujian. There is no place to shower or shelter from the rain. It is not as good as Shanghai, where Western missionaries have built small shelters from the rain. They do not know a single word of social education. I believe that since Nanyang relies on the labor of workers to develop, it should at least consider the lives and health of the lower classes. Places for workers to shower and shelter from the rain should be established everywhere. Japan even has drinking places for cattle and horses established throughout the streets. Does the wealth of Nanyang not match this? The greater the difference between the rich and poor classes, the more the feeling of class conflict will arise. We should reconcile them well, so as to eliminate the seeds of killing before they sprout. If we do not know how to seek social welfare and pursue the way of coexistence, it will be dangerous. Nanyang is gradually entering a Western capitalist lifestyle. The gap between rich and poor is too great. We should use Dr. Sun Yat-sen's plan for local autonomy and the Principle of People's Livelihood to make some adjustments. However, in the current schools, the British still restrict the Three Principles of the People and often send supervisors to check and prohibit them. However, the supervisors are still Chinese, covering their ears and stealing bells, just like the Manchus in the Qing Dynasty sent Han Chinese to investigate Han Chinese cases.

I once visited Nantong. Nantong has a worker education institution, worker residences, and nursing homes, homes for the blind and deaf, and orphanages. Although there are classes, there is still compassion and pity, which is more comforting than nothing. Now Nanyang is known for its capital wealth, but the lives of the lower-class workers are like this. How can we talk about autonomy, education, and health? There are often beggars and blind people begging for money on the streets.

27. I visited the Guanghui Zhao Hospital, which is run by the three counties of Guangzhou, Huizhou, and Zhaoqing. Staying means being hospitalized. The content and scale are quite impressive. There are three hundred men and women. It is clean with many trees. Those who die are provided with coffins and buried. But there is one drawback: because staying in the hospital is free, some people stay for as long as ten years. It is not a hospital but a nursing home. The name does not match the reality. The people in the hospital cannot remove them because they are kind-hearted and unwilling to kick them out. It is limited to people from the three counties, and people from other counties are not allowed. There is also a charge of one yuan per room per day to ensure special treatment. The long-term residents have no work to do and sit and wait for death. Is it not economical? We should use religion and art to purify their minds. Otherwise, eating and waiting for death is too bitter. Is it life? In short, it is difficult to talk about the middle way in the world. Competing will kill people. Talking about mercy and joy makes the hospital a nursing home, which is too good. I had a minor illness and received medicine as a gift, for which I am very grateful.

Today, science is prosperous, and superstition has long been broken. The story of foxes and ghosts is even less talked about. However, sometimes it also shows people strange news and events that make people half-believe and half-doubt. The following is a very detailed statement from a friend from the countryside. I will record it below:

In Yan Family Building in Liuzhao Bay, Nanyi Township, there is a famous "Little Granny" who has been working as a baby bather and midwife for more than thirty years. Late one night last month, she suddenly heard a knock on the door. She opened the door and saw two young girls who said they came from Er Tuan (about four or five miles away from Yan Family Building) and specially invited the old woman to deliver a baby. The woman did not suspect anything because of her profession and put on her clothes and went out. She saw a small boat waiting on the riverbank and went on the boat. The two young girls paddled and arrived in a moment. When she went ashore, she saw broken walls and scattered steps covered with fine grass. She entered a courtyard behind, and the stone road was smooth and no longer overgrown. She then arrived at the inner room and saw crystal curtains and embroidered screens with fragrant mist spraying people. When she asked the surname, they said it was Qu. The pregnant woman wore a red jacket and an embroidered skirt around her waist. She was in increasing pain and about to give birth. Soon she gave birth to a son. The woman bathed the baby and wrapped it up. She examined the dressing table and furnishings, which were extremely luxurious, knowing that it was a noble family. However, the lights in the room were the old oil lamps, and the light was unusually dim. Looking back at the pregnant woman, her face was like dust, and her pupils opened and closed from time to time, and her spirits seemed extremely tired. She exchanged pleasantries with the woman and ordered the two young girls to prepare dishes and entertain her. While she was staring, she suddenly saw a pair of red shoes on the head of the bed, each with a gold ingot attached, and she immediately became suspicious. Then she followed the girl and turned into the outer room, where dishes were lined up, which were quite delicious to eat. After the meal, she was given ten taels of gold as a reward and left. The two girls still sent her back on the original boat. In a moment, it was dawn. Her husband had already gotten up to cook and told her what he had seen and examined the money he had paid, which were all paper money for the dead. He couldn't help but be horrified. Her husband then ran to the riverbank, but the boat had disappeared. Afterwards, she told the neighbors, who were all amazed and said that the woman would not live long.

Short News The first Achievement Exhibition of the Changming Art School opened the day before yesterday. There were a total of more than 500 works, divided into six rooms for Chinese painting, calligraphy, seal carving, and Western painting. Overall, the works of the whole school can express special personalities, which is admirable. In the morning, there was drizzle, and fewer guests came. In the afternoon, it cleared up, and there was a steady stream of visitors. Many painting pieces were decided to be sold.

The towel has also been wiped, and the lemonade has also been delivered. The waiters know that Mr. Zuo is coming to book the room, and he can't be coming alone for a big meal. Zuo Shichen suddenly remembered the spirit of Li Taibai in the Kunqu Opera grinding ink for Gao Lishi, like a shadow passing through his heart. Looking at the pen in his hand, the tip of the pen seemed to be glued firmly with raw lacquer. He seemed to press it hard on the inkstone, and the tip of the pen shrank into the pen tube. He hid inside and refused to come out again. Poor Zuo Shichen was short-sighted. He thought he had already dipped it in ink and was about to wave his pen and write, but it was just a bare stick, a headless ghost. He wondered, "Hey, where did his head go?" In fact, the waiter grinding the ink saw it clearly and just bent over laughing, and said, "Mr. Zuo, change one." Then he handed over another pen. This one was also like a small broom. He thought that on ordinary days he would naturally write gambling tickets to summon Ruiyun. Today, he wanted to change his method and write a guest ticket to invite her. At the same time, they said to their patron, "Go right away, Mr. Zuo. Go right away. Our shop also knows Little Ruiyun. I'll tell them to give her the guest ticket if they run into her on the road." Zuo Shichen thought that writing the guest ticket was just a formality. He had already agreed to invite her without writing the guest ticket, and she would naturally come. At that time, he took out his watch and looked at it. It was already 7:30. But Ruiyun hadn't come yet. He thought that she would definitely come within this half hour anyway. Didn't Ajin just say on the phone that she would definitely arrive by 8 o'clock at the latest? A moment later, the person who sent the guest ticket came back and said that the guest ticket was sent to Qingfang, and they said that the person was not at home. She had gone to sing. But Zuo Shizhan felt that this half hour was longer than any other time. The waiters came to flatter him and said, "Mr. Zuo, do you want cigarettes?" One of the waiters said, "Zuo Xingkuang doesn't smoke cigarettes." Although Zuo Shichen didn't smoke cigarettes, he wanted to smoke one in this loneliness. He also remembered that Ruiyun often smoked cigarettes secretly to avoid her aunt's eyes. Today, for the sake of the dinner, he should also prepare some cigarettes.

U.S. Cotton Fabric Market Sluggish 180

Rayon Price Drops, Raw Cotton Affected

New York Telegraph on the 16th: The cotton fabric market is currently not very good, even worse than any period in the past two years. The only thing that excites the market is the slight increase in clothing sales. Cotton mills have been hearing about production cuts since early spring, but supply still far exceeds demand. Various cotton fabrics and many popular fabrics that have undergone finishing processes are now weak. This is proof that supply exceeds demand. Cotton manufacturers are now paying close attention to the price reductions of natural silk and rayon. Many people expect that lower silk prices will make cotton mills more inclined to produce rayon fabrics, as these fabrics are easier to sell and more profitable than cotton fabrics. Speakers are concerned about tariff issues, believing that tariffs will not only increase domestic competition but also cause other countries to take retaliatory actions, which will be detrimental to U.S. exports. The recent drop in the stock market and the continued downward trend in the prices of major commodities have caused a bleak atmosphere in the Wall Street market. The future outlook is currently uncertain.

Food Rice Market Continues to Rise 182

White Geng Rice Changes to Yuan, Rising Steadily

Yesterday, the source of river rice in Zhabei was scarce, and the stock was gradually thinning. The street market was quite brisk, and white geng rice rose by about 0.2 yuan again. The highest-grade top-quality geng rice requires 22 yuan, and the middle-quality geng rice from outside the customs is all around 21 yuan. However, the Social Affairs Bureau, in view of the recent rising rice prices, has strict restrictions. According to the white geng rice limit plate last month, it was relaxed to 21 yuan as the highest price limit. Now it has exceeded the price limit again. However, the stock of geng rice is exhausted, which is due to the fact that the market price of production and sales is not cost-effective. Transportation merchants and cargo customers are wary of the restrictions of the authorities and the cost of losses, so they are waiting and seeing without loading. This is the main reason for the recent scarcity of arrivals in this port. The fundamental solution is to first dredge the rice situation in the mainland, so that the source of supply in this port is uninterrupted, or it may be helpful. Thin rice is rising step by step, and all incoming goods are sold out. The top-quality goods require 21 yuan. It is seen that the corner and half of the sheep's horn tip have a few factory warehouses, and the ship goods are scarce. The sales are brisk, and the high-quality goods reach 20 yuan and change. The rising trend of Yuan has accelerated, because the market sales of customer firms are brisk, and the arrival of goods is scarce. The sellers have raised the price for sale, so the price has risen by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. At present, the top-quality change Yuan requires 18.8 yuan.

In South Shanghai, the number of river boats arriving is less than ten. The market is surprisingly brisk. The arrival of Changzhou-Wuxi northern geng rice is very rare, and most of the stock has also been sold out, so there is no standard market price. The route for Suzhou-Tongji machine-grown rice is extremely active, and the big market has risen by another 0.2 yuan, and the high-quality goods are gradually reaching the 20 yuan mark. However, the transaction prices in the market are different, and the restrictions of the Social Affairs Bureau are extremely strict. The sellers seem to be extremely worried, so the prices of top-quality goods from both the north and the south are not very accurate in recent days. The arrival of southern thin early rice is becoming less and less. The Ningbo and Tongzhou firms in this street are all concerned. The market is extremely brisk, and the market price is rising by the corner. The high-quality goods have already opened at more than 20 yuan. The stock of Tongbian rice is also scarce, and the price of guest Yuan also requires 18 yuan. The sales of Yin Yuan are especially brisk, and the price is also rising by the corner. Although the rice market is seeing continuous upward movement at the moment, the trend is still rising and not falling.

Early silkworms have fallen off, and cocoon production is decreasing. It is heard that only one or two cocoon shops have opened. The estimated price of cocoons will not exceed 40 yuan. Qingfeng Garden

Regarding "Xinyou" Chunsen 191

After reading the Xinyou Drama Society's "Letter Regarding the Difficult Drama Movement," I have a better understanding of the efforts of the Xinyou Drama Society and everything about them. Their "Motives for Holding the Difficult Drama Movement," "Planned Repertoire," "Various Difficulties During the Movement," "Results of the Movement," and "Our Future" are all faithfully and sincerely shown to us. I especially sympathize with the various difficulties that unfortunately occurred during this Difficult Drama Movement, and the other problems that followed from the difficulties were even more inevitable. However, this also made the outside world clearer about their spirit and perseverance in the New Art Drama Movement. Regarding the results of this movement, they themselves said, "We ourselves are very regretful, and everyone has a quite dissatisfied look on their faces, because we know our shortcomings best, and we have not achieved our ideals." Yes, the words of the Taoist immortal in Peach Blossom Spring still linger in my ears: "There is always higher than high, and better than better. Everything is endless. Even if we exhaust our life's energy, we cannot do it all." Then work hard, just as Mr. Yuan Muzhi has long told us, "In Napoleon's dictionary, there is no 'difficult.' In our dictionary, there is also no 'difficult.' In our dictionary, there is only 'do.'" Work hard, comrades, the future is not dark. We are willing to use our passionate enthusiasm as a kind of cotton force to assist and encourage each other, in an attempt to advance our drama movement. We thank the gentlemen of Xinyou for "We are always as hardworking as Miss Zou, as persevering as the Taoist immortal, and we will not disappoint him." This not only fills me with unspeakable gratitude and joy, but also inspires considerable respect from all friends who love drama. Now, I will briefly address their "Our Future" as a small contribution.

Indeed, during this movement, the small number of spectators made us doubt. In this modern era of unsound national spirit, "Uncle Vanya," "Dog's Dance," and "Peach Blossom Spring" are all targeted excitants. They truly gave us the power of the special functions of drama. Therefore, based on the script, Xinyou's selection of these three plays is valuable. Moreover, although Xinyou's performance art and stage skills have not yet reached perfection, they have already achieved considerable success.

I dare say that Mr. Yuan Muzhi's performance and makeup make him the only actor in China today. Other actors also have considerable training and cultivation. Here, I am not especially praising Mr. Yuan Muzhi. All friends who have seen him act say the same thing. Then, although the number of spectators is small and the economic distress may bring them to an unimaginable point, in the history of drama in the 19th year of the Republic, if the gentlemen who compile the history of drama do not wear colored glasses, they will surely leave a glorious history. Therefore, Xinyou's Difficult Drama Movement failed on the surface, but it greatly succeeded in reality. Moreover, "failure is the mother of success." Then, Xinyou's Difficult Drama Movement should be continued with effort. We are even more enthusiastically looking forward to Xinyou completing the Difficult Drama Movement project, arousing social belief and the sympathy of the audience from the partial to the whole. Xinyou's drama has not left the path of awakening the national spirit. Every play has a metaphor for awakening the nation. They are taking an absolutely correct direction. In my imagination, the public's understanding of valuable drama may not always be so superficial. If we do not relax our publicity efforts, they will definitely have a further understanding in the near future. We are very saddened that our drama circles are either falling into errors, simply insulting the original function of drama, only knowing to use it as a weapon for struggle and propaganda, and forgetting the mission of dramatic art, or they are still inevitably stuck in low-level tastes. Seeing Xinyou's three plays this time, the deep impression moved us, made us understand the true meaning of life, and made us open our minds and boldly take big strides on the journey of the enlightened life. In short, it is commendable to awaken and inspire our lazy national character. If the Xinyou Society changes the way of performing drama to make the audience have a general understanding, this opinion is of course very good. However, in the future, the selection of plays should be like "Uncle Vanya," "Dog's Dance," and "Peach Blossom Spring," focusing on the content of the play and concentrating on "national consciousness." This is the project that I hope Xinyou will continue to undertake.

Since Mr. Zhu Suicheng has this plan, it can be implemented as soon as possible. Finally, I look forward to the hard work of the Xinyou Drama Society.

May the gentlemen of Xinyou correct me.

(Attached Communication) Mr. Yuan Muzhi is the actor I love too much. When I truly appreciate and comprehend Mr. Yuan's performance, my emotions will flow with it. Although I have no opportunity to meet Mr. Yuan, I deeply believe in him. Now, I venture to ask Mr. Yuan to bestow his communication address so that I can go forward and ask for advice. Would this be a luxury? I hope that what you give me is not disappointment. Please send it to the Youth Garden Editorial Department of Shen Bao for forwarding. Respectfully, Chunsen.

"The Merchant of Venice" Will Be Revived 193

Among them, the Xinyou Drama Association's "The Merchant of Venice" has been the most praised by society. Disappointed Person 194

Inside that solemn and silent clinic, there was only one doctor and me, and a patient filled with panic sat on a chair. Because a doctor who understood a little Cantonese had gone out to see a patient, I was able to go to the clinic because I had received the doctor's order to go and temporarily act as an interpreter to convey opinions between the two parties.

As usual, the doctor asked her name, age, and address, and then asked about her past medical history. It turned out that she was a person who had just come out of the countryside. Because her husband often disagreed with her opinions, they often quarreled with each other. Therefore, she decided to try the life of a divorcee. Unfortunately, she lived in a friend's house in Shanghai for two months and learned that her body had changed. She also felt various phenomena such as loss of appetite, nausea, vomiting, and fatigue. With this obvious proof, she was even more worried about this little life. At the same time, thinking about her own future, she decided to sacrifice this little life.

However, this is not allowed by law. How can we violate the creed of humanitarianism for the sake of pitying her? The doctor simply and solemnly rejected the patient, but the patient begged extremely earnestly. In this dilemma, I also felt extremely difficult. I had no choice but to use some comforting words as a temporary relief. Unexpectedly, she used the catchphrase of the weak, saying that if it could not be done, she would rather die to cleanse everything about her. As she spoke, tears dripped down and finally she sobbed loudly.

"Don't cry. According to the doctor's examination results, it has not yet been determined that you are pregnant. Go back well, and don't make yourself seriously ill. After a month or two, you can come back here for an examination. I will pray for you, hoping that heaven will not be unfair, and hoping that the disappointed can be satisfied." I mustered up the courage to comfort her, and as a result, she also went back well. I watched the disappointed person's return journey in front of the school gate, and I fantasized about the mystery and ruggedness of life. (Bi Ling)

Automobile News

Special Commentary

Incomparably Precious, Exquisitely Unparalleled 195

Persian King's Royal Car Arrives

Commissioned from Studebaker's Pierce-Arrow Factory

King Reza Khan of Persia, in anticipation of the upcoming national celebrations, specifically commissioned a royal car from the Studebaker and Pierce-Arrow joint automobile factory in White Plains, New York, USA, to participate in parades and share joy with the people. Since accepting the commission, the factory, with its more than seventy years of automotive manufacturing experience, carefully designed and worked day and night to complete the car. It has now been fully completed and solemnly loaded for transport to Persia.

This car, gilded with gold, decorated with silver, inlaid with pearls and jade, is dazzling and incomparably luxurious. Although the time was pressing after its completion, and it was rushed for shipment without being displayed in America for an extended period, the two-day exhibition in New York already caused a sensation. It is estimated that more than 25,000 people visited, praising it and acknowledging its value.

According to a report by Ms. Della Meng published in World Travel Magazine, King of Persia is committed to reforms and striving for progress. His choice of Studebaker automobile for his use is enough to remind people of Persia's continuous renewal and eventual success. Although this custom-made royal car is one of the most luxurious and precious royal cars ever made, it is hardly representative of the daily life of the King of Persia. Although the King is the heir to all rights and wealth, he lives frugally. He always shares meals with the Queen, and the dishes are not delicacies and rarely exceed three bowls. He drinks moderately, smokes occasionally, and laughter fills the room, a truly exemplary family. The King is diligent in his duties and a model for his subjects. He rises at dawn every morning, exercises until six o'clock, and arrives at the office at eight o'clock. From eight to eleven-thirty, he receives his ministers and handles government affairs with utmost care, decisiveness, and solemnity. Afterwards, he retires for rest, either eating alone or with the Prince. At two o'clock, he continues to govern without interruption, year-round. He rarely hosts banquets for guests or officials, and even when he does, they are always filled with distinguished guests, never just one or two people, so as to save on expenses. Formal attire and all precious ornaments are never worn except at formal banquets. The King has no concubines but regards the Queen and children as his only companions. The King's new car is large and beautiful. The chassis is a standard Pierce-Arrow product with a wheelbase of 144 inches. The engine is a straight-eight cylinder type with 132 horsepower. The body construction is unprecedentedly luxurious. The exterior of the car is immaculate white, adding to its grandeur, and the gold trim makes it even more radiant and luxurious. The metal parts of the car, such as the mudguards, headlights, door panels, water tank, screen frame, bumper, and metal strips on the thick rubber running board, are all gilded, making them extremely luxurious. The double-sided car doors are engraved with artistic sculptures of the Persian royal crown, shining with golden light. The base of the crown is made of emerald green gemstones, complementing each other perfectly. The interior padding is made of light incense-colored silk fabric, embroidered with family crests and flower crowns, edged with gold and lined with white leather. The car window curtains are also made of silk fabric, decorated with lively patterns. The carpet on the floor of the car is made of wolfhound wool, specially selected from Russia. The cigarette holder and lighter are made of pure gold and inlaid with diamonds. The glass used in the car is all shatterproof. The front of the car, where the driver sits, is also splendid and exquisite. The dashboard and other parts are also plated with precious metals. The reason why the King of Persia specifically commissioned this car from the Studebaker and Pierce-Arrow joint automobile factory is that the factory's rich experience, high reputation, and the large number of high-end and luxurious cars it produces are recognized as leaders in the American automobile industry.

British Six-Wheeled Automobiles are Excellent and Abundantly Used by 196

Payne's Exploration and Land Reclamation

On June 6th of last year, the Australian government organized a desert expedition to find the bodies of two aviators. The purpose of these two aviators was to seek the Southern Cross constellation from Australia to London, but tragically, they went missing a few days after departure. Searching for the bodies of these two people in the wilderness is no easy task, as it requires crossing the barren northern land. It was finally decided to use a Thornycroft six-wheeled automobile with a three-ton payload as a means of transportation for this mission. The vehicle was loaded with three and a half tons of fuel, drinking water, food, personnel, and other supplies and set off from the inland station of Newcastle Waters directly into the vast desert. At the beginning, the vehicle traveled in low gear due to the loose soil. Later, encountering thickets of trees and grass, and due to tire damage, progress was delayed. On June 13th, they reached their destination, and the bodies of the two aviators were recovered at the same time. The return trip was much easier because there were existing tracks to follow, taking only two and a half days to return to the original starting point of Newcastle Waters. They then proceeded to Alice Springs Railway Station, and the remains of the two men were transported by train. In total, apart from some tire punctures and damages, there were no other difficulties along the way.

The above is just a glimpse of the use of British six-wheeled automobiles. This type of six-wheeled automobile is widely used and extremely important for road finding and exploration. It has long demonstrated its special functions in South America, South Africa, Canada, Iraq, and other places. In Australia, another six-wheeled automobile with a four-ton payload, named Albion, regularly travels between Sydney and Forbes in New South Wales, a distance of 300 miles. This journey is slightly different from others, as it must cross Mount Brolo, which is 4,000 feet above the ground. The entire round trip takes four days. Morris commercial six-wheeled automobiles, after completing tests in the tropical region of Quito, were tested on the old trails between Riobamba and Guaranda in the Andes Mountains. It has now been widened, but its slope remains the same as it has been for centuries, with only mules and horses traveling this road, carrying passengers and cargo. Now, Morris commercial automobiles regularly travel between the two cities, carrying twelve passengers and a half-ton of cargo, crossing the Andes' La Cumbre Pass, which is 4,200 meters above the ground, with slopes reaching about 30%.

In Canada, Thornycroft six-wheeled automobiles were tested in the northern Ontario mines, which were once icy and snowy lands. Previously, the only means of transportation were sleds and dog sleds. The entire journey was over 2,000 miles and took two weeks, progressing smoothly even when the temperature sometimes dropped to thirty degrees below zero. No mechanical adjustments were needed during the entire trip. For the companies involved in this test, it means that there can now be year-round automobile transportation to replace the American four-wheeled automobiles that can only operate for four months. When surveying the railway line between Rothsay and Walvis Bay in South Africa, Thornycroft six-wheeled automobiles were also used to cross the Kalahari Desert.
