Advantages of the Marmon Eight-Cylinder Car, Good People 198

The ratio of engine power to weight is related to the agility and sluggishness of a car's movements. Most vehicles must increase power with weight to perform adequately, but not Marmon automobiles. Increasing weight does not reduce power. These characteristics are the result of years of dedicated research and improvement by Marmon car engineers.

An engine with 50 horsepower driving a 2,000-pound car will be stronger than driving a 4,000-pound car. Driving a light car requires only one horsepower for every 40 pounds, while driving 80 pounds also uses one horsepower, so the difference in performance must be half as weak. The power-to-weight ratio of the 1930 Marmon automobiles is extremely remarkable, able to drive twice the weight without reducing power, adding comfort, luxury, and agility, which are the advantages of this new type of car.

The Marmon Big Eight-Cylinder car has an engine power of 125 horsepower, and each horsepower can tow 34.09 pounds of weight. The Marmon No. 79 Big Eight-Cylinder car has 107 horsepower, and each horsepower can tow 36.06 pounds of weight. The power-to-weight ratio of the Marmon No. 69 is one horsepower for every 36.09 pounds of weight. The Marmon R-Type engine has 77 horsepower, each horsepower for every 36.08 pounds of weight. The Marmon No. 69 engine also has great horsepower, with 84 horsepower.

The Marmon automobile engine is suitable for large cylinders. Marmon engineers have carefully modified it through years of field testing, resulting in today's most exquisite mechanical movement, excellent power-to-weight ratio, high speed, and quiet operation. The new Marmon four types of automobiles in 1930 are inexpensive and of good quality, and have now arrived in Shanghai. You are welcome to visit and test drive the car, which is currently managed by the Shanghai Haifeng Automobile Company.

Translated Compilation

World Automobile News 199

The Number of Automobiles in Various Countries is Increasing, and the Automobile Industry in the United States is Advancing Rapidly. The United States has always ranked first in the world for the number of automobiles domestically. In recent years, the number of automobiles in other countries has also been increasing. According to last year's statistics, excluding the United States, the total number of licensed automobiles in the world has increased by 16.5% compared to the previous year. There are now four countries with more than one million automobiles. The total number of automobiles, trucks, and long-distance automobiles in the world is an astonishing 32 million. The place with the fewest automobiles in the world is the Solomon Islands in the South Pacific, with only two automobiles. In terms of population ratio, excluding the United States, New York ranks second, with an average of one automobile for every nine people. Canada ranks third, with a maximum of one car for every nine people. As for the large number of automobiles in the United States, it accounts for 77% of the world's total, and its production accounts for 83.5% of the world's output because Europe only produced 600,000 automobiles last year.

Five Commissioners Go to the United States to Investigate Road Administration. Recently, more and more countries have sent commissioners to the United States to investigate road administration. Commissioners from Manila, Germany, Austria, Japan, and Finland have successively come to the United States to investigate road construction systems and automobile development plans in order to improve transportation. In addition, the United States' road administration tax, automobile donations, and vehicle management methods are also complete and unparalleled, and are what commissioners from various countries want to study.

News of Road Construction in South America. Mr. Rice, Associate of the American General Motors Company, recently returned from investigating road administration in various South American countries. According to him, the roads in major cities have mostly become accessible in all directions in the past four years, and there are also roads in the deep forests. Last year, South American countries convened a road administration conference to discuss methods of connecting main roads.

Long-Distance Automobile Travel in Chile. Three Chilean automobile enthusiasts traveled by car from Lima for 1,800 miles. Only a small part of the area they passed through had roads, and the rest were high mountains or wilderness. It took 35 days to reach their destination.

Last Year's Profits of American Factories 200

Ms. Cui Yin

The American automobile industry is the leading industry in the world, and the number of automobile manufacturers is as numerous as the sands of the Ganges River. People who care about the world's automobile industry are eager to know the profit reports of various automobile factories last year. Here are the translated reports that have been published:

(1) General Motors Factory. General Motors has been popular around the world in recent years and can compete with Ford. Its profits are self-evident.

Recently Transported General Motors Trucks to China 201

The American General Motors Company recently received 60 General Motors trucks shipped from the American headquarters to China and are currently temporarily stored at the Da Lai Steamship Company's wharf.

In the middle ear, the total profit in 1929 was US$488,256,392, an increase of more than double compared to the profit of US$235,104,826 in 1927.

(2) Dodge Factory. The total profit in 1929 was US$18,843,570. After deducting all taxes and other expenses, the preferred stock can receive a dividend of US$10.50 per share, and the common stock has a net profit of US$2.35 per share.

(3) Studebaker Factory. The American headquarters' net profit in 1929 was US$9,835,660, with a dividend of US$5.05 per share. The branch factories in various places have not yet been officially announced.

(4) Franklin Factory. The total profit in 1929 was US$135,798. After deducting taxes, the net profit per share was US$1.20.

(5) Hudson Factory. The total profit from 1929 to October 31 was US$11,437,552, with a net profit of US$6.40 per share.

(6) Packard Factory. Packard's profits from the Detroit factory alone have been announced, with a total profit of US$8,458,566. The common stock can receive a dividend of US$3.00 per share.

(7) Le Premier Factory. After deducting taxes and all expenses, the net profit in 1929 was US$639,164, with a dividend of US$2.50 per share.

(8) Mack Truck Factory. The pure profit in 1929 was US$6,043,105. Excluding the preferred stock dividend, each share was allocated a surplus of US$5.28.
